Page 1
Saudi Arabia 
Coordinates: [URL: "https://geohack.toolforge.org/geohack.php?pagename=Saudi_Arabia&params=24_N_45_E_type:country_region:SA"] 24°N 45°E
Saudi Arabia,[c] officially the Kingdom of Saudi Arabia
 (KSA),[d] is a country on the Arabian Peninsula in Western
Asia. It has a land area of about 2,150,000 km2
(830,000 sq mi), making it the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Asian_countries_by_area"] fifth-largest country in Asia,
the second-largest in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_world"] Arab world, and the largest in
Western Asia. It is bordered by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Sea"] Red Sea to the west;
Jordan, Iraq, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait"] Kuwait to the north; the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_Gulf"] Persian Gulf,
 Qatar and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates"] United Arab Emirates to the east; [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oman"] Oman to the
southeast; and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yemen"] Yemen to the south. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bahrain"] Bahrain is an island
country off the east coast. The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_of_Aqaba"] Gulf of Aqaba in the
northwest separates Saudi Arabia from Egypt. Saudi Arabia
is the only country with a coastline along both the Red Sea
and the Persian Gulf, and most of its terrain consists of arid
 desert, lowland, steppe, and mountains. Its capital and largest
city is Riyadh. The country is home to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mecca"] Mecca and Medina,
the two [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holiest_sites_in_Islam"] holiest cities in Islam.
 Pre-Islamic Arabia, the territory that constitutes modern-day
Saudi Arabia, was the site of several ancient cultures and
civilizations; the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prehistory_of_Saudi_Arabia"] prehistory of Saudi Arabia shows some of
the earliest traces of human activity in the world.[16] The
world's second-largest religion,[17] Islam, emerged in what is
now Saudi Arabia. In the early 7th century, the Islamic
prophet [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhammad"] Muhammad united the population of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabia"] Arabia and
created a single Islamic religious polity.[18] Following his
death in 632, his followers rapidly expanded the territory
 under Muslim rule beyond Arabia, conquering huge and
 unprecedented swathes of territory (from the Iberian
Peninsula in the west to parts of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Asia"] Central and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Asia"] South Asia in
the east) in a matter of decades. Arab dynasties originating
from modern-day Saudi Arabia founded the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rashidun_Caliphate"] Rashidun (632–
661),  [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Umayyad_Caliphate"] Umayyad (661–750),  [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abbasid_Caliphate"] Abbasid (750–1517),  and
 Fatimid (909–1171) caliphates, as well as numerous other
dynasties in Asia, Africa, and Europe.
The area of modern-day Saudi Arabia formerly consisted of
mainly four distinct historical regions: Hejaz, Najd, and parts
of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Arabia"] Eastern Arabia (Al-Ahsa) and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_Arabia"] Southern Arabia ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%27Asir_Region"] 'Asir).[19]
The Kingdom of Saudi Arabia was founded in 1932 by
King Abdulaziz (known as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ibn_Saud"] Ibn Saud in the West). He united
the four regions into a single state through a series of
conquests beginning in 1902 with the capture of Riyadh, the
ancestral home of his family, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Saud"] Al Saud. Saudi Arabia has
since been an [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Absolute_monarchy"] absolute monarchy, where the king, the
princes of the large Al Saud royal family and the country’s
traditional elites have overseen a highly authoritarian
regime.[20][21][22] The ultraconservative [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wahhabi"] Wahhabi religious
movement within [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sunni_Islam"] Sunni Islam has been described as a
"predominant feature of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi_culture"] Saudi culture",[20][21] although the
power of the religious establishment has been significantly

Page 2
eroded in the 2010s.[23] In its [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basic_Law_of_Saudi_Arabia"] Basic Law, Saudi Arabia
continues to define itself as a sovereign Arab [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_state"] Islamic state
with Islam as its official religion, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabic_language"] Arabic as its official
language, and Riyadh as its capital. Saudi Arabia is
sometimes called "the Land of the Two Holy Mosques" in
 reference to Al-Masjid al-Haram (in Mecca) and Al-Masjid
an-Nabawi (in Medina), the two holiest places in Islam.
Petroleum was discovered on 3 March 1938 and followed
up by several other finds in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Province,_Saudi_Arabia"] Eastern Province.[24][25]
Saudi Arabia has since become the world's second-largest oil
producer (behind the US) and the world's largest oil
exporter, controlling the world's second-largest oil reserves
and the sixth largest gas reserves.[26] The kingdom is
categorized as a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Bank_high-income_economy"] World Bank high-income economy with a
very high [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_Development_Index"] Human Development Index[27] and is the only
Arab country to be part of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/G20_major_economies"] G20 major economies.[28][29]
The kingdom spends 8% of its [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GDP"] GDP on the military (highest
in the world after Oman),[30] which places it as the world's
third biggest military spender behind the United States and
China,[31] and the world's largest arms importer from 2015
to 2019, receiving half of all the US arms exports to the
Middle East.[32][33] According to the BICC, Saudi Arabia is
the 28th most militarized country in the world and possesses
the second-best military equipment qualitatively in the
region, after Israel.[34] By the late 2010s, there have been
continual calls for halting of arms sales to Saudi Arabia,
mainly due to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi_Arabian-led_intervention_in_Yemen#Reports_of_war_crimes"] alleged war crimes in Yemen[35] and
 especially following the assassination of Jamal
Khashoggi.[36][37] The state has attracted criticism for a
variety of reasons, including its [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi_Arabian-led_intervention_in_Yemen"] role in the Yemeni Civil War,
 alleged sponsorship of Islamic terrorism and its poor human
rights record, which has been characterized by the excessive
and often extrajudicial [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capital_punishment_in_Saudi_Arabia"] use of capital punishment,[38] failure
to adopt adequate measures against [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_trafficking_in_Saudi_Arabia"] human trafficking, state-
sponsored [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freedom_of_religion_in_Saudi_Arabia"] discrimination against religious minorities and
atheists,[39][40] and antisemitism, and its strict interpretation
of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sharia_law"] Sharia law.[41][42]
Saudi Arabia is considered both a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regional_power"] regional and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_power"] middle
power.[43][44] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi_economy"] Saudi economy is the largest in the
Middle East and eighteenth-largest in the world.[45] Saudi
Arabia also has one of the world's youngest populations,
with approximately 50 per cent of its population of 34.2
million being under 25 years old.[46] In addition to being a
member of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_Cooperation_Council"] Gulf Cooperation Council, Saudi Arabia is an
active and founding member of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations"] United Nations,
 Organisation of Islamic Cooperation, Arab League, Arab
Air Carriers Organization and OPEC.

Etymology
Following the amalgamation of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hejaz"] Kingdom of Hejaz and Nejd, the new state was named al-Mamlakah al-
ʿArabīyah as-Suʿūdīyah (a transliteration of ‎السعودية ‎العربية ‎المملكة in Arabic) by royal decree on 23 September
1932 by its founder, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ibn_Saud"] Abdulaziz bin Saud. Although this is normally translated as "the Kingdom of Saudi Arabia" in
Page 4
English,[47] it literally means "the Saudi Arab kingdom",[48] or "the Arab Saudi Kingdom".[49]
The word "Saudi" is derived from the element as-Saʿūdīyah in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabic_language"] Arabic name of the country, which is a type of
adjective known as a nisba, formed from the dynastic name of the Saudi royal family, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/House_of_Saud"] Al Saud (Arabic: ‎سعود ‎آل).
Its inclusion expresses the view that the country is the personal possession of the royal family.[50][51] Al Saud is an
 Arabic name formed by adding the word Al, meaning "family of" or "House of",[52] to the personal name of an
ancestor. In the case of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Saud"] Al Saud, this is [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saud_ibn_Muhammad_ibn_Muqrin"] Saud ibn Muhammad ibn Muqrin, the father of the dynasty's 18th-century
founder, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhammad_bin_Saud"] Muhammad bin Saud.[53]
History
Prehistory
There is evidence that human habitation in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula"] Arabian Peninsula dates back to
about 125,000 years ago.[54] A 2011 study found that the first modern humans to
 spread east across Asia left Africa about 75,000 years ago across the Bab-el-
Mandeb connecting the Horn of Africa and Arabia.[55] The Arabian peninsula is
regarded as a central figure in the understanding of hominin evolution and
dispersals. Arabia underwent an extreme environmental fluctuation in the
 Quaternary that led to profound evolutionary and demographic changes. Arabia
has a rich [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lower_Paleolithic"] Lower Paleolithic record, and the quantity of Oldowan-like sites in the
region indicate a significant role that Arabia had played in the early hominin
colonization of Eurasia.[56]
In the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neolithic"] Neolithic period, prominent cultures such as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Magar"] Al-Magar, whose centre lay in
modern-day southwestern Najd flourished. Al-Magar could be considered a
"Neolithic Revolution" in human knowledge and handicraft skills.[57] The culture
is characterized as being one of the world's first to involve the widespread
domestication of animals, particularly the horse, during the Neolithic
period.[58][59] Aside from horses, animals such as sheep, goats, dogs, in particular
of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saluki"] Saluki breed, ostriches, falcons and fish were discovered in the form of
stone statues and rock engravings. Al-Magar statues were made from local stone,
and it seems that the statues were fixed in a central building that might have had a
significant role in the social and religious life of the inhabitants.[60] 
Anthropomorphic stela (4th
millennium BC), sandstone,
57x27 cm, from El-Maakir-
 Qaryat al-Kaafa (National
Museum of Saudi Arabia,
Riyadh)
 In November 2017, hunting scenes showing images of the most likely domesticated dogs, resembling the Canaan
dog, wearing leashes were discovered in Shuwaymis, a hilly region of northwestern Saudi Arabia. These rock
engravings date back more than 8,000 years, making them the earliest depictions of dogs in the world.[61]
At the end of the 4th millennium BC, Arabia entered the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bronze_Age"] Bronze Age after witnessing drastic transformations; metals
were widely used, and the period was characterized by its 2 m high burials which were simultaneously followed by
the existence of numerous temples, that included many free-standing sculptures originally painted with red
colours.[62]
In May 2021, archaeologists announced that a 350,000-year-old [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Acheulean"] Acheulean site named An Nasim in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%E1%B8%A4a%CA%BCil_Province"] Hail region
could be the oldest human habitation site in northern Saudi Arabia. The site was first discovered in 2015 using remote
sensing and palaeohydrological modelling. It contains paleolake deposits related with [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Pleistocene"] Middle Pleistocene materials.
354 artefacts, hand axes and stone tools, flakes discovered by researchers provided information about tool-making
traditions of the earliest living man inhabited South-West Asia. Besides, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paleolithic"] Paleolithic artefacts are similar to material
remains uncovered at the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Acheulean"] Acheulean sites in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/An_Nafud"] Nefud Desert.[63][64][65][66]
Pre-Islamic
Page 5
The earliest sedentary culture in Saudi Arabia dates back to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ubaid_period"] Ubaid period, upon
discovering various pottery sherds at Dosariyah. Initial analysis of the discovery
concluded that the eastern province of Saudi Arabia was the homeland of the earliest
settlers of Mesopotamia, and by extension, the likely origin of the Sumerians.
However, experts such as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joan_Oates"] Joan Oates had the opportunity to see the Ubaid period
sherds in eastern Arabia and consequently conclude that the sherds date to the last
two phases of the Ubaid period (period three and four), while a handful of examples
could be classified roughly as either Ubaid 3 or Ubaid 2. Thus, the idea that colonists
from Saudi Arabia had emigrated to southern Mesopotamia and founded the region's
first sedentary culture was abandoned.[68]
Climatic change and the onset of aridity may have brought about the end of this phase
of settlement, as little archaeological evidence exists from the succeeding
millennium.[69] The settlement of the region picks up again in the period of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dilmun"] Dilmun in
the early 3rd millennium. Known records from [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uruk"] Uruk refer to a place called Dilmun,
associated on several occasions with copper, and in later periods it was a source of
imported woods in southern Mesopotamia. A number of scholars have suggested that
Dilmun originally designated the eastern province of Saudi Arabia, notably linked
with the major Dilmunite settlements of Umm an-Nussi and Umm ar-Ramadh in the
interior and Tarout on the coast. It is likely that [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tarout_Island"] Tarout Island was the main port and
the capital of Dilmun.[67] Mesopotamian inscribed clay tablets suggests that, in the

statue (2500 BC), above one

early period of Dilmun, a form of hierarchical organized political structure existed. In
1966, an earthwork in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tarout"] Tarout exposed an ancient burial field that yielded a large, impressive statue dating to the
Dilmunite period (mid 3rd millennium BC). The statue was locally made under the strong Mesopotamian influence
on the artistic principle of Dilmun.[67]
By 2200 BC, the centre of Dilmun shifted for unknown reasons from Tarout and the Saudi Arabian mainland to the
island of Bahrain, and a highly developed settlement emerged there, where a laborious temple complex and thousands
of burial mounds dating to this period were discovered.[67]
Qaṣr Al-Farīd, the largest of the 131
 rock-cut monumental tombs built
from the 1st century BC to the 1st
century AD, with their elaborately
ornamented façades, at the
extensive ancient [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nabatean"] Nabatean
archaeological site of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hegra_(Mada%27in_Salih)"] Hegra located
 in the area of Al-'Ula within Al
Madinah Region in the Hejaz. A
UNESCO [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Heritage_Site"] World Heritage Site since
2008. 
By the late Bronze Age, a historically recorded people and land (Midian and
the Midianites) in the north-western portion of Saudi Arabia are well-
documented in the Bible. Centred in Tabouk, it stretched from [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wadi_Arabah"] Wadi Arabah
in the north to the area of al-Wejh in the south.[70] The capital of Midian was
Qurayyah,[71] it consists of a large fortified citadel encompassing 35 hectares
and below it lies a walled settlement of 15 hectares. The city hosted as many
as 10 to 12 thousand inhabitants.[72] The Midianites were depicted in two
major events in the Bible that recount Israel's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Midian_war"] two wars with Midian,
somewhere in the early 11th century BC. Politically, the Midianites were
described as having a decentralized structure headed by five kings (Evi,
Rekem, Tsur, Hur, and Reba), the names appears to be toponyms of important
Midianite settlements.[73] It is common to view that Midian designated a
confederation of tribes, the sedentary element settled in the Hijaz while its
nomadic affiliates pastured, and sometimes pillaged as far away land as
Palestine.[74] The nomadic Midianites were one of the earliest exploiters of
the domestication of camels that enabled them to navigate through the harsh
terrains of the region.[74]
At the end of the 7th century BC, an emerging kingdom appeared in the
historical theatre of north-western Arabia. It started as a Sheikdom of Dedan,
which developed into the Kingdom of Lihyan tribe.[75] The earliest attestation of state regality, King of Lihyan, was
in the mid-sixth century BC.[76] The second stage of the kingdom saw the transformation of Dedan from a mere city-
state of which only influence they exerted was inside their city walls, to a kingdom that encompasses much wider
domain that marked the pinnacle of Lihyan civilization.[75] The third state occurred during the early 3rd century BC
with bursting economic activity between the south and north that made Lihyan acquire large influence suitable to its
strategic position on the caravan road.[77]
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hejaz"]
Page 6
Lihyan was a powerful and highly organized ancient [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabian"] Arabian kingdom that played a
vital cultural and economic role in the north-western region of the Arabian
Peninsula.[78] The Lihyanites ruled over a large domain from [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medina"] Yathrib in the south and
parts of the Levant in the north.[79] In antiquity, Gulf of Aqaba used to be called Gulf
of Lihyan. A testimony to the extensive influence that Lihyan acquired.[80]
The Lihyanites fell into the hands of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nabataeans"] Nabataeans around 65 BC upon their seizure
of Hegra then marching to Tayma, and to their capital Dedan in 9 BC. The
Nabataeans ruled large portions of north Arabia until their domain was annexed by
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Empire"] Roman Empire, which renamed it [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabia_Petraea"] Arabia Petraea, and remained under the rule of
the Romans until 630.[81]

peninsula and created a single Islamic religious polity.[18] Following his death
in 632, his followers rapidly expanded the territory under Muslim rule beyond
Arabia, conquering huge and unprecedented swathes of territory (from the
Iberian Peninsula in the west to parts of Central and South Asia in the east) in
a matter of decades. Arabia soon became a more politically peripheral region
of the Muslim world as the focus shifted to the vast and newly conquered
lands.[18]
than any previous empire in history. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab"] Arabs originating from modern-day Saudi Arabia, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hejaz"] Hejaz in particular,
founded the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rashidun_Caliphate"] Rashidun (632–661),  [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Umayyad_Caliphate"] Umayyad (661–750),  [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abbasid_Caliphate"] Abbasid (750–
1517), and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fatimid_Caliphate"] Fatimid (909–1171) caliphates. From the 10th century to the
early 20th century, Mecca and Medina were under the control of a local Arab ruler known as the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sharif_of_Mecca"] Sharif of Mecca, but
at most times the Sharif owed allegiance to the ruler of one of the major Islamic empires based in Baghdad, Cairo or
Istanbul. Most of the remainder of what became Saudi Arabia reverted to traditional tribal rule.[85][86]
For much of the 10th century, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isma%27ilism"] Isma'ili-Shi'ite [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qarmatians"] Qarmatians were the most powerful
force in the Persian Gulf. In 930, the Qarmatians pillaged Mecca, outraging the
Muslim world, particularly with their theft of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_Stone"] Black Stone.[87] In 1077–1078, an
Arab Sheikh named [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abdullah_bin_Ali_Al_Uyuni"] Abdullah bin Ali Al Uyuni defeated the Qarmatians in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Arabia"] Bahrain
 and al-Hasa with the help of the Great Seljuq Empire and founded the Uyunid
dynasty.[88][89] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uyunid_Emirate"] Uyunid Emirate later underwent expansion with its territory
stretching from Najd to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syrian_desert"] Syrian desert.[90] They were overthrown by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Usfurids"] Usfurids
in 1253.[91] Usfurid rule was weakened after Persian rulers of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ormus"] Hormuz captured
Bahrain and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qatif"] Qatif in 1320.[92] The vassals of Ormuz, the Shia [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jarwanid_dynasty"] Jarwanid dynasty
came to rule eastern Arabia in the 14th century.[93][94] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jabrids"] Jabrids took control of the
region after overthrowing the Jarwanids in the 15th century and clashed with Hormuz
for more than two decades over the region for its economic revenues, until finally
agreeing to pay [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tribute"] tribute in 1507.[93] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Muntafiq"] Al-Muntafiq tribe later took over the region and
came under [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_Empire"] Ottoman suzerainty. The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bani_Khalid"] Bani Khalid tribe later revolted against them in
the 17th century and took control.[95] Their rule extended from Iraq to Oman at its
height and they too came under Ottoman suzerainty.[96][97] 
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Badr"] Battle of Badr, 13
March 624 CE
Ottoman Hejaz
Page 7
In the 16th century, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottomans"] Ottomans added the Red Sea and Persian Gulf coast (the Hejaz, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%27Asir_Province"] Asir and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Arabia"] Al-Ahsa) to the
Empire and claimed [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suzerainty"] suzerainty over the interior. One reason was to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_naval_expeditions_in_the_Indian_Ocean"] thwart Portuguese attempts to attack the Red Sea
(hence the Hejaz) and the Indian Ocean.[98] The Ottoman degree of control over these lands varied over the next four
centuries with the fluctuating strength or weakness of the Empire's central authority.[99][100] These changes
contributed to later uncertainties, such as the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Occupation_of_Ma%27an"] dispute with Transjordan over the inclusion of the sanjak of Ma'an,
including the cities of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ma%27an"] Ma'an and Aqaba.
Foundation of the Saud dynasty
The emergence of what was to become the Saudi royal family, known as the
Al Saud, began in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nejd"] Nejd in central Arabia in February 1727,[101][102] when
 Muhammad bin Saud, founder of the dynasty, joined forces with the religious
leader [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhammad_ibn_Abd_al-Wahhab"] Muhammad ibn Abd al-Wahhab,[103] founder of the Wahhabi
movement, a strict puritanical form of Sunni Islam.[104] This alliance formed
in the 18th century provided the ideological impetus to Saudi expansion and
remains the basis of Saudi Arabian dynastic rule today.[105]
In 1727, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emirate_of_Diriyah"] Emirate of Diriyah established in the area around Riyadh rapidly
expanded and briefly controlled most of the present-day territory of Saudi
Arabia,[106] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wahhabi_sack_of_Karbala"] sacking Karbala in 1802, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Destruction_of_early_Islamic_heritage_sites_in_Saudi_Arabia"] capturing Mecca in 1803. In 1818,
 it was destroyed by the Ottoman viceroy of Egypt, Mohammed Ali 
Atlas map of Arabia and the wider
region in 1883
Pasha.[107] The much smaller [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emirate_of_Nejd"] Emirate of Nejd was established in 1824.
Throughout the rest of the 19th century, the Al Saud contested control of the interior of what was to become Saudi
Arabia with another Arabian ruling family, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rashidi_dynasty"] Al Rashid, who ruled the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emirate_of_Jabal_Shammar"] Emirate of Jabal Shammar. By 1891, the Al
Rashid were victorious and the Al Saud were driven into exile in Kuwait.[85]
At the beginning of the 20th century, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_Empire"] Ottoman Empire continued to
control or have a suzerainty over most of the peninsula. Subject to this
suzerainty, Arabia was ruled by a patchwork of tribal rulers,[108][109] with the
 Sharif of Mecca having pre-eminence and ruling the Hejaz.[110] In 1902,
 Abdul Rahman's son, Abdul Aziz—later to be known as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ibn_Saud"] Ibn Saud—
recaptured control of Riyadh bringing the Al Saud back to Nejd, creating the
 third "Saudi state".[85] Ibn Saud gained the support of the Ikhwan, a tribal
army inspired by Wahhabism and led by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Faisal_Al-Dawish"] Faisal Al-Dawish, and which had
grown quickly after its foundation in 1912.[111] With the aid of the Ikhwan,
Ibn Saud captured Al-Ahsa from the Ottomans in 1913.
In 1916, with the encouragement and support of Britain (which was fighting
the Ottomans in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I"] World War I), the Sharif of Mecca, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_Sharif_of_Mecca"] Hussein bin Ali, led a
 pan-Arab revolt against the Ottoman Empire to create a united Arab
state.[112] Although the Arab Revolt of 1916 to 1918 failed in its objective,
 the Allied victory in World War I resulted in the end of Ottoman suzerainty
and control in Arabia and Hussein bin Ali became [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hejaz"] King of Hejaz.[113] 
 Abdulaziz Ibn Saud, the founding
father and first king of Saudi Arabia
Ibn Saud avoided involvement in the Arab Revolt, and instead continued his
struggle with the Al Rashid. Following the latter's final defeat, he took the title [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sultanate_of_Nejd"] Sultan of Nejd in 1921. With the help
of the Ikhwan, the Kingdom of Hejaz was conquered in 1924–25, and on 10 January 1926, Ibn Saud declared
himself King of Hejaz.[114] For the next five years, he administered the two parts of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hejaz_and_Nejd"] his dual kingdom as separate
units.[85]
After the conquest of the Hejaz, the Ikhwan leadership's objective switched to expansion of the Wahhabist realm into
the British protectorates of Transjordan, Iraq and Kuwait, and began raiding those territories. This met with Ibn
Saud's opposition, as he recognized the danger of a direct conflict with the British. At the same time, the Ikhwan
became disenchanted with Ibn Saud's domestic policies which appeared to favour modernization and the increase in
the number of non-Muslim foreigners in the country. As a result, they turned against Ibn Saud and, after a two-year
Page 8
struggle, were defeated in 1929 at the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Sabilla"] Battle of Sabilla, where their leaders were massacred.[115] On 23 September
1932, the two [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hejaz_and_Nejd"] kingdoms of the Hejaz and Nejd were united as the Kingdom of Saudi Arabia,[85] and that date is now
a national holiday called [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi_National_Day"] Saudi National Day.[116]
Post-unification
The new kingdom was reliant on limited agriculture and pilgrimage
revenues.[117] In 1938, vast reserves of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Petroleum"] oil were discovered in the Al-Ahsa
region along the coast of the Persian Gulf, and full-scale development of the
 oil fields began in 1941 under the US-controlled Aramco (Arabian American
Oil Company). Oil provided Saudi Arabia with economic prosperity and
substantial political leverage internationally.[85]
Cultural life rapidly developed, primarily in the Hejaz, which was the centre
 for newspapers and radio. However, the large influx of foreign workers in
Saudi Arabia in the oil industry increased the pre-existing propensity for
xenophobia.[118] At the same time, the government became increasingly
wasteful and extravagant. By the 1950s this had led to large governmental
deficits and excessive foreign borrowing.[85] 
Political map of Saudi Arabia
In 1953, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saud_of_Saudi_Arabia"] Saud of Saudi Arabia succeeded as the king of Saudi Arabia, on his
father's death, until 1964 when he was deposed in favour of his half brother
 Faisal of Saudi Arabia, after an intense rivalry, fuelled by doubts in the royal family over Saud's competence. In 1972,
Saudi Arabia gained a 20 per cent control in Aramco, thereby decreasing US control over Saudi oil.
In 1973, Saudi Arabia led an oil boycott against the Western countries that supported Israel in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War"] Yom Kippur War
 against Egypt and Syria. Oil prices quadrupled.[85] In 1975, Faisal was assassinated by his nephew, Prince Faisal bin
Musaid and was succeeded by his half-brother [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khalid_of_Saudi_Arabia"] King Khalid.[119]
By 1976, Saudi Arabia had become the largest oil producer in the world.[120] Khalid's reign saw economic and social
development progress at an extremely rapid rate, transforming the infrastructure and educational system of the
country;[85] in foreign policy, close ties with the US were developed.[119] In 1979, two events occurred which greatly
concerned the government,[121] and had a long-term influence on Saudi foreign and domestic policy. The first was
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_Revolution"] Iranian Islamic Revolution. It was feared that the country's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shi%27a_Islam_in_Saudi_Arabia"] Shi'ite minority in the Eastern Province (which is also
the location of the oil fields) might rebel under the influence of their Iranian co-religionists. There were several anti-
government uprisings in the region such as the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1979_Qatif_Uprising"] 1979 Qatif Uprising.[122]
The second event was the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grand_Mosque_Seizure"] Grand Mosque Seizure in Mecca by Islamist extremists. The militants involved were in
part angered by what they considered to be the corruption and un-Islamic nature of the Saudi government.[122] The
government regained control of the mosque after 10 days and those captured were executed. Part of the response of
the royal family was to enforce the much stricter observance of traditional religious and social norms in the country
(for example, the closure of cinemas) and to give the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ulema"] Ulema a greater role in government.[123] Neither entirely
succeeded as Islamism continued to grow in strength.[124]
In 1980, Saudi Arabia bought out the American interests in Aramco.[125] King Khalid died of a heart attack in June
1982. He was succeeded by his brother, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fahd_of_Saudi_Arabia"] King Fahd, who added the title "Custodian of the Two Holy Mosques" to his
name in 1986 in response to considerable fundamentalist pressure to avoid the use of "majesty" in association with
anything except God. Fahd continued to develop close relations with the United States and increased the purchase of
American and British military equipment.[85]
The vast wealth generated by oil revenues was beginning to have an even greater impact on Saudi society. It led to
rapid technological (but not cultural) modernization, urbanization, mass public education, and the creation of new
media. This and the presence of increasingly large numbers of foreign workers greatly affected traditional Saudi
norms and values. Although there was a dramatic change in the social and economic life of the country, political
power continued to be monopolized by the royal family[85] leading to discontent among many Saudis who began to
look for wider participation in government.[126]
Page 9
In the 1980s, Saudi Arabia spent $25 billion in support of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saddam_Hussein"] Saddam Hussein in
 the Iran–Iraq War;[127] however, Saudi Arabia condemned the Iraqi invasion
of Kuwait in 1990 and asked the US to intervene.[85] King Fahd allowed
American and coalition troops to be stationed in Saudi Arabia. He invited the
Kuwaiti government and many of its citizens to stay in Saudi Arabia, but
expelled citizens of Yemen and Jordan because of their governments' support
of Iraq. In 1991, Saudi Arabian forces were involved both in bombing raids
on Iraq and in the land invasion that helped to liberate Kuwait.
Saudi Arabia's relations with the West began to cause growing concern
among some of the ulema and students of Sharia law and was one of the
issues that led to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_militant_incidents_in_Saudi_Arabia"] an increase in Islamist terrorism in Saudi Arabia, as well as
 Islamist terrorist attacks in Western countries by Saudi nationals. Osama bin
Map of Saudi Arabian administrative
regions and roadways 
Laden was a Saudi citizen (until stripped of his citizenship in 1994) and was
responsible for the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1998_U.S._embassy_bombings"] 1998 U.S. embassy bombings in East Africa and the 2000
 USS Cole bombing near the port of Aden, Yemen. 15 of the 19 terrorists
involved in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/September_11_attacks"] September 11 attacks in New York City, Washington, D.C., and
near Shanksville, Pennsylvania were Saudi nationals.[128] Many Saudis who did not support the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamist"] Islamist terrorists
were nevertheless deeply unhappy with the government's policies.[129]
Islamism was not the only source of hostility to the government. Although extremely wealthy by the 21st century,
Saudi Arabia's economy was near stagnant. High taxes and a growth in unemployment have contributed to discontent
and have been reflected in a rise in civil unrest, and discontent with the royal family. In response, a number of limited
reforms were initiated by King Fahd. In March 1992, he introduced the "[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basic_Law_of_Saudi_Arabia"] Basic Law", which emphasized the duties
and responsibilities of a ruler. In December 1993, the Consultative Council was inaugurated. It is composed of a
chairman and 60 members—all chosen by the King. The King's intent was to respond to dissent while making as few
actual changes in the status quo as possible. Fahd made it clear that he did not have democracy in mind, saying: "A
system based on elections is not consistent with our Islamic creed, which [approves of] government by consultation
[shūrā]."[85]
In 1995, Fahd suffered a debilitating stroke, and the Crown Prince, Abdullah, assumed the role of de facto regent,
taking on the day-to-day running of the country; however, his authority was hindered by conflict with Fahd's full
brothers (known, with Fahd, as the "[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sudairi_Seven"] Sudairi Seven").[130] From the 1990s, signs of discontent continued and
included, in 2003 and 2004, a series of bombings and armed violence in Riyadh, Jeddah, Yanbu and Khobar.[131] In
February–April 2005, the first-ever nationwide municipal elections were held in Saudi Arabia. Women were not
allowed to take part in the poll.[85]
In 2005, King Fahd died and was succeeded by Abdullah, who continued the
policy of minimum reform and clamping down on protests. The king
introduced a number of economic reforms aimed at reducing the country's
reliance on oil revenue: limited deregulation, encouragement of foreign
investment, and privatization. In February 2009, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abdullah_of_Saudi_Arabia"] Abdullah announced a series
of governmental changes to the judiciary, armed forces, and various ministries
to modernize these institutions including the replacement of senior appointees
in the judiciary and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_religious_police"] Mutaween (religious police) with more moderate
individuals and the appointment of the country's first female deputy
minister.[85]
On 29 January 2011, hundreds of protesters gathered in the city of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jeddah"] Jeddah in
a rare display of criticism against the city's poor infrastructure after deadly
floods swept through the city, killing 11 people.[132] Police stopped the
demonstration after about 15 minutes and arrested 30 to 50 people.[133] 
Map of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Petroleum"] oil and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_gas"] gas pipelines in the
Middle-East
Since 2011, Saudi Arabia has been affected by its own [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2011%E2%80%9313_Saudi_Arabian_protests"] Arab Spring protests.[134] In response, King Abdullah
announced on 22 February 2011 a series of benefits for citizens amounting to $36 billion, of which $10.7 billion was
earmarked for housing.[135][136][137] No political reforms were announced as part of the package, though some
prisoners indicted for financial crimes were pardoned.[138] On 18 March the same year, King Abdullah announced a
Page 10
package of $93 billion, which included 500,000 new homes to a cost of $67 billion, in addition to creating 60,000
new security jobs.[139][140] Although male-only [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi_Arabian_municipal_elections,_2011"] municipal elections were held on 29 September 2011,[141][142]
Abdullah allowed women to vote and be elected in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi_Arabian_municipal_elections,_2015"] 2015 municipal elections, and also to be nominated to the
 Shura Council.[143]
Since 2001, Saudi Arabia has engaged in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Censorship_in_Saudi_Arabia#The_Internet"] widespread internet censorship. Most online censorship generally falls into
two categories: one based on censoring "immoral" (mostly pornographic and LGBT-supportive websites along with
 websites promoting any religious ideology other than Sunni Islam) and one based on a blacklist run by Saudi Arabia's
Ministry of Media, which primarily censors websites critical of the Saudi regime or associated with parties that are
opposed to or opposed by Saudi Arabia.[144][145][146]
Politics 
Saudi Arabia is an [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Absolute_monarchy"] absolute monarchy;[147] however, according to
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basic_Law_of_Saudi_Arabia"] Basic Law of Saudi Arabia adopted by royal decree in 1992,
the king must comply with [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sharia"] Sharia (Islamic law) and the Quran,
while the Quran and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sunnah"] Sunnah (the traditions of Muhammad) are
declared to be the country's constitution.[148] No political parties
or national elections are permitted.[147] Saudi Arabia is
authoritarian,[149][150][151] and some critics regard it as a
 totalitarian state.[152][153][154] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Economist"] The Economist rated the Saudi
 Salman bin Abdulaziz Al [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohammad_bin_Salman"] Mohammad bin
Saud  Salman 
government as the fifth most authoritarian government out of 167
rated in its 2012 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democracy_Index"] Democracy Index,[155] and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freedom_House"] Freedom House gave
 King and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Saudi_Arabia"] Prime Minister [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crown_Prince_of_Saudi_Arabia"] Crown Prince and  it its lowest "Not Free" rating, 7.0 ("1=best, 7=worst") for
First Deputy Prime 2019.[156]
Minister 
In the absence of national elections and political parties,[147]
politics in Saudi Arabia takes place in two distinct arenas: within
the royal family, the Al Saud, and between the royal family and the rest of Saudi society.[157] Outside of the Al-Saud,
participation in the political process is limited to a relatively small segment of the population and takes the form of the
royal family consulting with the ulema, tribal sheikhs, and members of important commercial families on major
decisions.[158] This process is not reported by the Saudi media.[159]
By custom, all males of full age have a right to petition the king directly through the traditional tribal meeting known
as the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Majlis"] majlis.[160] In many ways the approach to government differs little from the traditional system of tribal rule.
Tribal identity remains strong and, outside of the royal family, political influence is frequently determined by tribal
affiliation, with tribal sheikhs maintaining a considerable degree of influence over local and national events.[158] As
mentioned earlier, in recent years there have been limited steps to widen political participation such as the
establishment of the Consultative Council in the early 1990s and the National Dialogue Forum in 2003.[161]
 The rule of the Al Saud faces political opposition from four sources: Sunni Islamist activism; liberal critics; the Shi'ite
minority—particularly in the Eastern Province; and long-standing tribal and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regionalism_(politics)"] regionalist particularistic opponents (for
example in the Hejaz).[162] Of these, the minority activists have been the most prominent threat to the government
and have in recent years perpetrated a number of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_militant_incidents_in_Saudi_Arabia"] violent incidents in the country.[131] However, open protest against
the government, even if peaceful, is not tolerated.[163]
Monarchy and royal family
The king combines legislative, executive, and judicial functions[158] and royal decrees form the basis of the country's
legislation.[164] The king is also the prime minister, and presides over the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Council_of_Ministers_of_Saudi_Arabia"] Council of Ministers of Saudi Arabia and
 Consultative Assembly of Saudi Arabia. The royal family dominates the political system. The family's vast numbers
allow it to control most of the kingdom's important posts and to have an involvement and presence at all levels of
government.[165] The number of princes is estimated to be at least 7,000, with most power and influence being
wielded by the 200 or so male descendants of Ibn Saud.[166] The key ministries are generally reserved for the royal
family,[147] as are the 13 regional governorships.[167]
Page 11
Long-term political and government appointments have resulted in the
creation of "power fiefdoms" for senior princes,[168] such as those of King
Abdullah, who had been Commander of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi_Arabian_National_Guard"] National Guard since 1963 (until
 2010, when he appointed his son to replace him),[169] former Crown Prince
Sultan, Minister of Defence and Aviation from 1962 to his death in 2011,
former crown prince [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nayef_bin_Abdul_Aziz"] Prince Nayef who was the Minister of Interior from
1975 to his death in 2012, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saud_bin_Faisal_bin_Abdulaziz_Al_Saud"] Prince Saud who had been Minister of Foreign
Affairs since 1975[170] and current [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salman_bin_Abdulaziz_Al_Saud"] King Salman, who was Minister of
Defense and Aviation before he was crown prince and Governor of the
 Riyadh Province from 1962 to 2011.[171] The current Minister of Defense is
 Prince Mohammad bin Salman, the son of King Salman and Crown
Prince.[172] 
 King Fahd with US President Ronald
Reagan and future US President
 Donald Trump in 1985. The US and
 Saudi Arabia supplied money and
The royal family is politically divided by factions based on clan loyalties,
personal ambitions and ideological differences.[157] The most powerful clan 
arms to the anti-Soviet [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mujahideen"] mujahideen
fighters in Afghanistan.
faction is known as the '[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sudairi"] Sudairi Seven', comprising the late King Fahd and
his full brothers and their descendants.[173] Ideological divisions include
issues over the speed and direction of reform,[174] and whether the role of the ulema should be increased or reduced.
There were divisions within the family over who should succeed to the throne after the accession or earlier death of
Prince Sultan.[173][175] When prince Sultan died before ascending to the throne on 21 October 2011, King Abdullah
appointed Prince Nayef as crown prince.[176] The following year, Prince Nayef also died before ascending to the
throne.[177]
As many as 500 princes,
government ministers, and business
 people, including Prince Fahd bin
Abdullah, were arrested by Saudi
Arabian authorities as part of the
 2017 Saudi Arabian purge 
The Saudi government[178][179][180] and the royal family[181][182][183] have
often been accused of corruption over many years,[184] and this continues
into the 21st century.[185] In a country that is said to "belong" to the royal
family and is [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Etymology_of_Saudi_Arabia"] named for them,[51] the lines between state assets and the
personal wealth of senior princes are blurred.[166] The extent of corruption
has been described as systemic[186] and endemic,[187] and its existence was
acknowledged[188] and defended[189] by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bandar_bin_Sultan"] Prince Bandar bin Sultan (a senior
member of the royal family)[190] in an interview in 2001.[191] Although
corruption allegations have often been limited to broad undocumented
accusations,[192] specific allegations were made in 2007, when it was claimed
that the British defence contractor [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BAE_Systems"] BAE Systems had paid Prince Bandar
US$2 billion in bribes relating to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Yamamah_arms_deal"] Al-Yamamah arms deal.[193][194] Prince
Bandar denied the allegations.[195] In 2010, investigations by both US and
UK authorities resulted in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plea_bargain"] plea bargain agreements with the company, by
which it paid $447 million in fines but did not admit to bribery.[196]
In its [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Corruption_Perceptions_Index"] Corruption Perceptions Index for 2010, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transparency_International"] Transparency International gave Saudi Arabia a score of 4.7 (on a scale
from 0 to 10 where 0 is "highly corrupt" and 10 is "highly clean").[197] Saudi Arabia has undergone a process of
political and social reform, such as to increase public transparency and good governance, but nepotism and patronage
are widespread when doing business in the country; the enforcement of the anti-corruption laws is selective and
public officials engage in corruption with impunity. A number of prominent Saudi Arabian princes, government
ministers, and businesspeople, including Prince [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Waleed_bin_Talal"] Al-Waleed bin Talal, were [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2017_Saudi_Arabian_anti-corruption_arrests"] arrested in Saudi Arabia in November
2017.[198]
There has been mounting pressure to reform and modernize the royal family's rule, an agenda championed by King
Abdullah both before and after his accession in 2005. The creation of the Consultative Council in the early 1990s did
not satisfy demands for political participation, and, in 2003, an annual National Dialogue Forum was announced that
would allow selected professionals and intellectuals to publicly debate current national issues, within certain
prescribed parameters. In 2005, the first municipal elections were held. In 2007, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allegiance_Council"] Allegiance Council was created
to regulate the succession.[161] In 2009, the king made significant personnel changes to the government by appointing
reformers to key positions and the first woman to a ministerial post;[199][200] however, these changes have been
criticized as being too slow or merely cosmetic.[201]
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Secretary_of_Defense_Chuck_Hagel_walks_with_Saudi_Deputy_Minister_of_Defense_Prince_Fahd_bin_Abdullah_before_departing_Riyadh,_Saudi_Arabia,_on_April_24,_2013_130424-D-BW835-179.jpg"]
Page 12
Al ash-Sheikh and role of the ulema
Saudi Arabia is almost unique in giving the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ulama"] ulema (the body of Islamic
religious leaders and jurists) a direct role in government.[202] The preferred
ulema are of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salafi_movement"] Salafi persuasion. The ulema have also been a key influence
 in major government decisions, for example the imposition of the oil embargo
in 1973 and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_War"] invitation to foreign troops to Saudi Arabia in 1990.[203] In
addition, they have had a major role in the judicial and education systems[204]
and a monopoly of authority in the sphere of religious and social morals.[205] 
 Abdullah ibn Muhammad Al ash-
By the 1970s, as a result of oil wealth and the modernization of the country Sheikh with [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bogdan_Borusewicz"] Bogdan Borusewicz in
initiated by King Faisal, important changes to Saudi society were underway
and the power of the ulema was in decline.[206] However, this changed 
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_Senate"] Polish Senate, 26 May 2014
following the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grand_Mosque_Seizure"] seizure of the Grand Mosque in Mecca in 1979 by Islamist
radicals.[207] The government's response to the crisis included strengthening the ulema's powers and increasing their
financial support:[123] in particular, they were given greater control over the education system[207] and allowed to
enforce the stricter observance of Wahhabi rules of moral and social behaviour.[123] After his accession to the throne
in 2005, King Abdullah took steps to reduce the powers of the ulema, for instance transferring control over girls'
education to the Ministry of Education.[208]
The ulema have historically been led by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_ash-Sheikh"] Al ash-Sheikh,[209] the country's leading religious family.[205] The Al
ash-Sheikh are the descendants of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhammad_ibn_Abd_al-Wahhab"] Muhammad ibn Abd al-Wahhab, the 18th-century founder of the Wahhabi form of
Sunni Islam which is today dominant in Saudi Arabia.[210] The family is second in prestige only to the Al Saud (the
royal family)[211] with whom they formed a "mutual support pact"[212] and power-sharing arrangement nearly 300
years ago.[203] The pact, which persists to this day,[212] is based on the Al Saud maintaining the Al ash-Sheikh's
authority in religious matters and upholding and propagating Wahhabi doctrine. In return, the Al ash-Sheikh support
the Al Saud's political authority[213] thereby using its religious-[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moral_authority"] moral authority to legitimize the royal family's
rule.[214] Although the Al ash-Sheikh's domination of the ulema has diminished in recent decades,[215] they still hold
the most important religious posts and are closely linked to the Al Saud by a high degree of intermarriage.[205]
Legal system
The primary source of law is the Islamic [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sharia"] Sharia derived from the teachings of
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qur%27an"] Qur'an and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sunnah"] Sunnah (the traditions of the Prophet).[164] Saudi Arabia is
unique among modern Muslim states in that Sharia is not codified and there is
no system of judicial precedent, giving judges the power to use independent
legal reasoning to make a decision. Saudi judges tend to follow the principles
of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hanbali"] Hanbali school of jurisprudence ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fiqh"] fiqh) found in pre-modern texts[217]
and noted for its literalist interpretation of the Qur'an and hadith.[218]
Because the judge is empowered to disregard previous judgments (either his
own or of other judges) and may apply his personal interpretation of Sharia to
any particular case, divergent judgments arise even in apparently identical
cases,[219] making predictability of legal interpretation difficult.[220] The
Sharia court system constitutes the basic judiciary of Saudi Arabia and its
judges (qadi) and lawyers form part of the ulema, the country's Islamic
scholars.[221] 
Verses from the Quran. The Quran is
the official constitution of the country
and a primary source of law. Saudi
Arabia is unique in enshrining a
religious text as a political
document.[216]
Royal decrees are the other main source of law; but are referred to as regulations rather than laws because they are
subordinate to the Sharia.[164] Royal decrees supplement Sharia in areas such as labour, commercial and corporate
law. Additionally, traditional tribal law and custom remain significant.[222] Extra-Sharia government tribunals usually
handle disputes relating to specific royal decrees.[223] Final appeal from both Sharia courts and government tribunals
is to the King and all courts and tribunals follow Sharia rules of evidence and procedure.[224]
Page 13
The Saudi system of justice has been criticized for its "ultra-puritanical judges", who are often harsh in their
sentencing (with beheading for the crime of witchcraft), but also sometimes overly lenient (for cases of rape or wife-
beating) and slow, for example leaving thousands of abandoned women unable to secure a divorce.[225][226] The
system has also been criticized for being arcane,[227] lacking in some of the safeguards of justice, and unable to deal
with the modern world.[228]In 2007, King Abdullah issued royal decrees reforming the judiciary and creating a new
court system,[219] and, in 2009, the King made a number of significant changes to the judiciary's personnel at the
most senior level by bringing in a younger generation.[227] Studies have shown that Saudi Arabia has one of the
lowest crime rates in the world although there are differing views as to whether this is attributable to the legal system
or other factors such as social structures.[229]Although repeated theft can be punishable by amputation of the right
hand, only one instance of judicial amputation was reported between 2007[230] and 2010.[231][232][233] Atheism or
"calling into question the fundamentals of the Islamic religion on which this country is based" is considered a terrorist
crime.[234]Lashings are a common form of punishment[235] and are often imposed for offences against religion and
public morality such as drinking alcohol and neglect of prayer and fasting obligations.[236]
Retaliatory punishments, or Qisas, are practised: for instance, an eye can be surgically removed at the insistence of a
victim who lost his own eye.[226] Families of someone unlawfully killed can choose between demanding the death
penalty or granting clemency in return for a payment of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diyya"] diyya (blood money), by the perpetrator.[237]
Foreign relations 
Saudi Arabia joined the UN in 1945[47][238] and is a founding member of the
 Arab League, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cooperation_Council_for_the_Arab_States_of_the_Gulf"] Gulf Cooperation Council, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muslim_World_League"] Muslim World League, and the
 Organisation of the Islamic Conference (now the Organisation of Islamic
 Cooperation).[239] It plays a prominent role in the International Monetary
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Trade_Organization"] Fund and the World Bank, and in 2005 joined the World Trade
 Organization.[47] Saudi Arabia supports the intended formation of the Arab
Customs Union in 2015 and an Arab [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Single_market"] common market[240] by 2020, as
U.S. President [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump"] Donald Trump and  announced at the 2009 Arab League summit.[241]
First Lady [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Melania_Trump"] Melania Trump with King
 Salman bin Abdulaziz Al Saud and
 the President of Egypt, Abdel Fattah
Al Sisi, 21 May 2017 
Since 1960, as a founding member of OPEC, its oil pricing policy has been
generally to stabilize the world oil market and try to moderate sharp price
movements so as to not jeopardize the Western economies.[47][242] In 1973,
Saudi Arabia and other Arab nations imposed an [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oil_embargo"] oil embargo against the
United States, United Kingdom, Japan and other Western nations which
supported [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel"] Israel in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War"] Yom Kippur War of October 1973.[243] The embargo caused an [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1973_oil_crisis"] oil crisis with many short- and
long-term effects on global politics and the global economy.[244]
Between the mid-1970s and 2002, Saudi Arabia expended over $70 billion in "overseas development aid". However,
there is evidence that the vast majority was, in fact, spent on propagating and extending the influence of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wahhabism"] Wahhabism
at the expense of other forms of Islam.[245] There has been an intense debate over whether Saudi aid and Wahhabism
has fomented extremism in recipient countries.[246] The two main allegations are that, by its nature, Wahhabism
encourages intolerance and promotes terrorism.[247] Counting only the non-Muslim-majority countries, Saudi Arabia
has paid for the construction of 1359 mosques, 210 Islamic centres, 202 colleges, and 2000 schools.[248]
 Saudi Arabia and the United States are strategic allies,[249][250] and since President [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama"] Barack Obama took office in
2009, the US has sold $110 billion in arms to Saudi Arabia.[251] However, the relationship between Saudi Arabia and
 the United States became strained and have witnessed major decline during the last years of the Obama
administration,[252][253][254] although Obama had authorized US forces to provide logistical and intelligence support
to the Saudis in their [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi_Arabian-led_intervention_in_Yemen"] military intervention in Yemen, establishing a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blockade_of_Yemen#United_States's_role"] joint coordination planning cell with the Saudi
military that is helping manage the war,[255][256] and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CIA"] CIA used Saudi bases for [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Disposition_Matrix"] drone assassinations in
Yemen.[257][258][259][260] In the first decade of the 21st century the Saudi Arabia paid approximately $100 million to
 American firms to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi_Arabia_lobby_in_the_United_States"] lobby the U.S. government.[261] On 20 May 2017, President [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump"] Donald Trump and King Salman
signed a series of letters of intent for Saudi Arabia to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2017_United_States%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_arms_deal"] purchase arms from the United States totalling US$110 billion
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qisas"]
Page 14
immediately and $350 billion over 10 years.[262][263] In December 2021, the
US Senate voted against a proposal to stop a $650 million sales of advanced
medium range air-to-air missiles to Saudi Arabia to discourage it from its
military intervention in Yemen.[264][265]

 China and Saudi Arabia are major allies, with relationship between the two
countries growing significantly in recent decades. A significant number of
Saudi Arabians have also expressed a positive view of China.[271][272][273]
 In February 2019, Crown Prince Mohammad defended China's Xinjiang re-
education camps for [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uyghurs"] Uyghur Muslims,[274][275] saying "China has the right to carry out anti-terrorism and de-
extremisation work for its national security."[276][277] In July 2019, UN ambassadors of 37 countries, including Saudi
Arabia, have signed a joint letter to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UNHRC"] UNHRC defending China's treatment of Uyghurs and other Muslim minority
groups in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xinjiang"] Xinjiang region.[278]
The consequences of the 2003 invasion and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Spring"] Arab Spring led to increasing alarm within the Saudi monarchy over
the rise of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran"] Iran's influence in the region.[279] These fears were reflected in comments of King Abdullah,[208] who
privately urged the United States to attack Iran and "cut off the head of the snake".[280] The tentative rapprochement
between the US and Iran that began in secret in 2011[281] was said to be feared by the Saudis,[282] and, during the
run up to the widely welcomed deal on Iran's nuclear programme that capped the first stage of US–Iranian détente,
Robert Jordan, who was US ambassador to Riyadh from 2001 to 2003, said "[t]he Saudis' worst nightmare would be
the [Obama] administration striking a grand bargain with Iran."[283] A trip to Saudi by US President Barack Obama
in 2014 included discussions of US–Iran relations, though these failed to resolve Riyadh's concerns.[284]
In order to protect the house of Khalifa, the monarchs of Bahrain, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi-led_intervention_in_Bahrain"] Saudi Arabia invaded Bahrain by sending military
troops to quell the uprising of Bahraini people on 14 March 2011.[285] The Saudi government considered the two-
month uprising as a "security threat" posed by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia_Islam"] Shia who represent the majority of Bahrain population.[285]
On 25 March 2015, Saudi Arabia, spearheading a coalition of Sunni Muslim
states,[286] started a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi_Arabian-led_intervention_in_Yemen"] military intervention in Yemen against the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia_Islam"] Shia [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Houthis"] Houthis
and forces loyal to former President [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ali_Abdullah_Saleh"] Ali Abdullah Saleh, who was deposed in
the 2011 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Spring"] Arab Spring uprisings.[287] At least 56,000 people have been killed
in armed violence in Yemen between January 2016 and October 2018.[288]
 Saudi Arabia, together with Qatar and Turkey, openly supported the Army of
Conquest,[289][290] an umbrella group of anti-government forces fighting in
 the Syrian Civil War that reportedly included an al-Qaeda linked al-Nusra
Front and another [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salafi_jihadism"] Salafi coalition known as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ahrar_al-Sham"] Ahrar al-Sham.[291] Saudi
Arabia was also involved in the CIA-led [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timber_Sycamore"] Timber Sycamore covert operation
to train and arm [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_armed_groups_in_the_Syrian_Civil_War"] Syrian rebels.[292] 
Foreign Minister [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adel_al-Jubeir"] Adel al-Jubeir with
 then British Foreign Secretary Boris
Johnson (now [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom"] Prime Minister) in
London, 16 October 2016
Page 15
Following a number of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Incidents_during_the_Hajj"] incidents during the Hajj season, the deadliest[293] of which killed at least 2,070 pilgrim[294]
in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2015_Mina_stampede"] 2015 Mina stampede, Saudi Arabia has been accused of mismanagement and focusing on increasing money
revenues while neglecting pilgrims' welfare.[295]
In March 2015, Sweden scrapped an arms deal with Saudi Arabia, marking an end to a decade-old defence
agreement with the kingdom. The decision came after Swedish Foreign Minister [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Margot_Wallstr%C3%B6m"] Margot Wallstrom was blocked by
the Saudis while speaking about democracy and women's rights at the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_League"] Arab League in Cairo. This also led to Saudi
Arabia recalling its ambassador to Sweden.[296]
Saudi Arabia has been seen as a moderating influence in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_conflict"] Arab–Israeli conflict, periodically putting forward a
peace plan between Israel and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_people"] Palestinians and condemning Hezbollah.[297] Following the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Spring"] Arab Spring Saudi
Arabia offered asylum to deposed President [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zine_El_Abidine_Ben_Ali"] Zine El Abidine Ben Ali of Tunisia and King Abdullah telephoned
President [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hosni_Mubarak"] Hosni Mubarak of Egypt (prior to his deposition) to offer his support.[298] In early 2014 relations with
 Qatar became strained over its support for the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muslim_Brotherhood"] Muslim Brotherhood, and Saudi Arabia's belief that Qatar was
interfering in its affairs. In August 2014 both countries appeared to be exploring ways of ending the rift.[299] Saudi
Arabia and its allies have criticized Qatar-based TV channel [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Jazeera"] Al Jazeera and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Qatar_relations"] Qatar's relations with Iran. In 2017,
Saudi Arabia imposed a land, naval and air [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_Qatar_diplomatic_crisis"] blockade on Qatar.[300]
Saudi Arabia halted new trade and investment dealings with Canada and
 suspended diplomatic ties in a dramatic escalation of a dispute over the
kingdom's arrest of women's rights activist [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samar_Badawi"] Samar Badawi on 6 August
2018.[301][302]
Tensions have escalated between Saudi Arabia and its allies after the
disappearance of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jamal_Khashoggi"] Jamal Khashoggi from the Saudi consulate in Istanbul.
Turkish officials are highly sceptical of Khashoggi being murdered inside the
 consulate; this has strained the already suffering Saudi Arabia–Turkey
relations. As stated by Ozgur Unluhisarcikli, director of the German Marshall
Fund's Ankara office "Turkey is maintaining a very delicate balance in its
relations with Saudi Arabia. The relations have the potential of evolving into
a crisis at any moment."[303]
