conflict locations
The pressure on Saudi to reveal the insights about [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Killing_of_Jamal_Khashoggi"] Khashoggi's disappearance from the US and other European
countries has increased. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi_Arabia%E2%80%93United_States_relations"] Saudi-US relations took an ugly turn on 14 October 2018, when Trump promised "severe
punishment" if the royal court was responsible for Khashoggis' death. The Saudi Foreign Ministry retaliated with an
equal statement saying, "it will respond with greater action," indicating the kingdom's "influential and vital role in the
global economy." A joint statement was issued by Britain, France, and Germany also demanding a "credible
investigation to establish the truth about what happened, and — if relevant — to identify those bearing responsibility
for the disappearance of Jamal Khashoggi, and ensure that they are held to account."[304]
The US expects its Gulf allies involved in the coalition in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yemen"] Yemen to put in more efforts and address the rising
concerns about the millions that have been pushed to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Famine_in_Yemen_(2016%E2%80%93present)"] brink of famine. According to the United Nations, the
Arabian peninsula nation is home to the world's worst humanitarian crisis.[305] More than 50,000 children in Yemen
died from [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Starvation"] starvation in 2017.[306] The famine in Yemen is the direct result of the Saudi-led intervention and blockade
of the rebel-held area.[307][308]
In the wake of Jamal Khashoggi's murder in October 2018, the US secretary of state [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mike_Pompeo"] Mike Pompeo and the US
defence secretary [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jim_Mattis"] Jim Mattis called for a ceasefire in Yemen within 30 days followed by UN-initiated peace talks.
Pompeo has asked Saudi Arabia and the UAE to stop their airstrikes on populated areas in Yemen. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theresa_May"] Theresa May
backed the US call to end the coalition. President of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Rescue_Committee"] International Rescue Committee [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Miliband"] David Miliband called the
US announcement as "the most significant breakthrough in the war in Yemen for four years".[309]
In September 2020, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Showtime_(TV_network)"] Showtime announced that it will premiere its original documentary, Kingdom of Silence, on 2
October that year. The film was based on the 2018 murder of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jamal_Khashoggi"] Jamal Khashoggi by Saudi authorities. Directed by
filmmaker Rick Rowley, the documentary examines the relationship between the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States"] US and Saudi Arabia, as a backdrop
Page 16
to the murder of Khashoggi, along with the interactions between the Trump administration and Saudi Crown Prince
Mohammed bin Salman.[310] Another documentary by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bryan_Fogel"] Bryan Fogel, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Dissident"] The Dissident, which excavated a web of deceit
behind the murder, was to be released on the same day that marked the second death anniversary of Khashoggi.[311]
 Jeremy Hunt, the UK Foreign Secretary, on his visit to Saudi Arabia and the UAE on 12 November 2018, is
expected to raise the need for a ceasefire from all sides in the four-year-long Yemen civil war. The US called for a
 ceasefire within 30 days.[312] Andrew Smith, of Campaign Against Arms Trade (CAAT), said that Hunt and Boris
Johnson "played an utterly central and complicit role in arming and supporting the Saudi-led destruction of
Yemen."[313][314]
In 2017, as part of its nuclear power program, Saudi Arabia planned to extract uranium domestically, taking a step
towards self-sufficiency in producing [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_fuel"] nuclear fuel. On 24 August 2017, the Kingdom signed a memorandum of
understanding with [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/China_National_Nuclear_Corporation"] China National Nuclear Corporation (CNNC) to explore and assess uranium[315] On 4 August
2020, a report claimed that Saudi Arabia has constructed a facility in the desert near Al-'Ula for extracting uranium
yellowcake from [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uranium_ore"] uranium ore with the help of China. The facility raised concerns among the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States"] US and allied officials
about Saudi nuclear energy plans and the country's option of developing [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_weapon"] nuclear weapon.[316] On 19 August 2020,
Congressional Democrats asked the US secretary of state, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mike_Pompeo"] Mike Pompeo, to provide information about China's
alleged role in building a uranium processing facility in Saudi Arabia.[317]
On 17 September 2020, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Guardian"] The Guardian released an exclusive report revealing that Saudi Arabia was paving the way
for domestic production of nuclear fuel. The confidential report obtained by the media house stated that the Kingdom
was assisted by Chinese geologists to produce over 90,000 tonnes of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uranium"] uranium from three major deposits in the centre
and northwest of Saudi, near the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NEOM"] NEOM megacity development. The disclosure raised concerns regarding Riyadh's
aggressive interest in developing atomic weapons program.[318] Apart from China, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UN"] UN nuclear watchdog,
 International Atomic Energy Agency (IAEA) was also assisting Saudi's nuclear ambition.[319]
Allegations of sponsoring global terrorism
According to the Iraqi prime minister [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nouri_al-Maliki"] Nouri al-Maliki in March 2014, Saudi
Arabia along with Qatar provided political, financial, and media support to
terrorists against the Iraqi government.[320] Similarly, President of Syria
 Bashar al-Assad noted that the sources of the extreme ideology of the terrorist
organization [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_State_of_Iraq_and_the_Levant"] ISIS and other such [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salafi_jihadism"] salafist extremist groups are the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wahabbism"] Wahabbism
that has been supported by the royal family of Saudi Arabia.[321]
Relations with the U.S. became strained following [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/September_11_attacks"] 9/11 terror attacks.[322]
American politicians and media accused the Saudi government of supporting
terrorism and tolerating a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jihadist"] jihadist culture.[323] Indeed, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osama_bin_Laden"] Osama bin Laden and
15 out of the 19 9/11 hijackers were from Saudi Arabia;[324] in ISIL-
occupied Raqqa, in mid-2014, all 12 judges were Saudi.[325] The leaked US 
Flag of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Qaeda"] Al-Qaeda, a transnational
 terrorist group formed by Osama bin
Laden, a Saudi Arabian national of
Yemeni and Syrian extraction who
was stripped of his Saudi passport in
1994.
Department of State memo, dated 17 August 2014, says that "governments of
Qatar and Saudi Arabia...are providing clandestine financial and logistic
 support to ISIS and other radical groups in the region."[254] According to former US Secretary of State Hillary
Clinton, "Saudi Arabia remains a critical financial support base for al-Qaida, the Taliban, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LeT"] LeT and other terrorist
groups...  Donors in Saudi Arabia constitute the most significant source of funding to Sunni terrorist groups
worldwide."[326] Former CIA director [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_Woolsey"] James Woolsey described it as "the soil in which [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Qaeda"] Al-Qaeda and its sister
terrorist organizations are flourishing."[327] The Saudi government denies these claims or that it exports religious or
cultural extremism.[328] In April 2016, Saudi Arabia has threatened to sell off $750 billion in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Treasury_security"] Treasury securities and
other US assets if [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Congress"] Congress passes a bill that would allow the Saudi government to be sued over 9/11.[249] In
September 2016, the Congress passed the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Justice_Against_Sponsors_of_Terrorism_Act"] Justice Against Sponsors of Terrorism Act that would allow relatives of
victims of the 11 September attacks to sue Saudi Arabia for its government's alleged role in the attacks.[329] Congress
overwhelmingly rejected President [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_United_States_presidential_vetoes"] Barack Obama's veto.[253][254]
According to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Patey"] Sir William Patey, former British ambassador to Saudi Arabia, the kingdom funds mosques throughout
Europe that have become hotbeds of extremism. "They are not funding terrorism. They are funding something else,
which may down the road lead to individuals being radicalised and becoming fodder for terrorism," Patey said. He
Page 17
said that Saudi has been funding an ideology that leads to extremism and the leaders of the kingdom are not aware of
the consequences.[330]
However, since 2016 the kingdom began backing away from Islamist ideologies.[331] Several reforms took place
including curbing the powers of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Committee_for_the_Promotion_of_Virtue_and_the_Prevention_of_Vice_(Saudi_Arabia)"] religious police,[332] stopping funding mosques in foreign countries,[333] and first
mixed-gender concert performed by woman.[334] In 2017, Saudi Crown Prince Mohammed bin Salman declared a
return to “moderate Islam”.[335]
Military 
 The Saudi military consists of the Royal Saudi Land Forces, the Royal Saudi
 Air Force, the Royal Saudi Navy, the Royal Saudi Air Defense, the Saudi
Arabian National Guard (SANG, an independent military force),  and
paramilitary forces, totalling nearly 200,000 active-duty personnel. In 2005
the armed forces had the following personnel: the army, 75,000; the air force,
"The Saudi pilots training in Italy
1935"—a scene from 'Our Eagles', 
18,000; air defence, 16,000; the navy, 15,500 (including 3,000 marines); and
the SANG had 75,000 active soldiers and 25,000 tribal levies.[336] In
addition, there is an [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Mukhabarat_Al_A%27amah"] Al Mukhabarat Al A'amah military intelligence service.
one of four [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Video_wall"] video wall shows made
for the Royal Saudi Air Force
Museum 
The kingdom has a long-standing military relationship with Pakistan, it has
 long been speculated that Saudi Arabia secretly funded Pakistan's atomic
bomb programme and seeks to purchase atomic weapons from Pakistan, in
near future.[337][338] The SANG is not a reserve but a fully operational front-
line force, and originated out of Ibn Saud's tribal military-religious force, the Ikhwan. Its modern existence, however,
is attributable to it being effectively [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abdullah_of_Saudi_Arabia"] Abdullah's private army since the 1960s and, unlike the rest of the armed forces,
is independent of the Ministry of Defense and Aviation. The SANG has been a counterbalance to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sudairi"] Sudairi faction
in the royal family: The late prince Sultan, former Minister of Defense and Aviation, was one of the so-called 'Sudairi
Seven' and controlled the remainder of the armed forces until his death in 2011.[339]
Spending on defence and security has increased significantly since the mid-
1990s and was about US$78.4 billion, as of 2019.[31] Saudi Arabia has one
of the highest percentages of military expenditure in the world, spending
around 8% of its GDP in its military, according to the 2020 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stockholm_International_Peace_Research_Institute"] SIPRI
estimate.[340] Its modern high-technology arsenal makes Saudi Arabia among
the world's most densely armed nations, with its military equipment being
supplied primarily by the US, France, and Britain.[336]
The United States sold more than $80 billion in military hardware between
1951 and 2006 to the Saudi military.[341] On 20 October 2010, the US State
Department notified Congress of its intention to make the biggest arms sale in 
Saudi soldiers from the First Airborne
Brigade.
American history—an estimated $60.5 billion purchase by the Kingdom of
Saudi Arabia. The package represents a considerable improvement in the offensive capability of the Saudi armed
forces.[342] 2013 saw Saudi military spending climb to $67bn, overtaking that of the UK, France and Japan to place
fourth globally.[343]
The United Kingdom has also been a major supplier of military equipment to Saudi Arabia since 1965.[344] Since
1985, the UK has supplied military aircraft—notably the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Panavia_Tornado"] Tornado and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eurofighter_Typhoon"] Eurofighter Typhoon combat aircraft—and
other equipment as part of the long-term [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Yamamah_arms_deal"] Al-Yamamah arms deal estimated to have been worth £43 billion by 2006
and thought to be worth a further £40 billion.[345] In May 2012, British defence giant BAE signed a £1.9bn ($3bn)
deal to supply Hawk trainer jets to Saudi Arabia.[346]
According to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stockholm_International_Peace_Research_Institute"] Stockholm International Peace Research Institute, SIPRI, in 2010–14 Saudi Arabia became the
world's second-largest arms importer, receiving four times more major arms than in 2005–2009. Major imports in
2010–14 included 45 combat aircraft from the UK, 38 combat helicopters from the US, four tanker aircraft from
Spain, and over 600 armoured vehicles from Canada. Saudi Arabia has a long list of outstanding orders for arms,
including 27 more combat aircraft from the UK, 154 combat aircraft from the US, and a large number of armoured
Page 18
vehicles from Canada.[347] Saudi Arabia received 41 per cent of UK arms exports in 2010–14.[348] France
authorized $18 billion in weapons sales to Saudi Arabia in 2015 alone.[251] The $15 billion arms deal with Saudi
Arabia is believed to be the largest arms sale in Canadian history.[349] In 2016, the European Parliament decided to
temporarily impose an arms embargo against Saudi Arabia, as a result of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yemen"] Yemen civilian population's suffering
 from the conflict with Saudi Arabia.[350] In 2017, Saudi Arabia signed a 110 billion dollar arms deal with the United
States.
Saudi Arabia is Britain's largest arms customer, with more than £4.6 billion worth of arms bought since the start of
Saudi-led coalition in Yemen. A recent poll conducted by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/YouGov"] YouGov for Save the Children and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avaaz"] Avaaz stated that 63 per
cent of British people oppose the sale of weapons to Saudi.[351]
Following the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Killing_of_Jamal_Khashoggi"] killing of Jamal Khashoggi, a nonbinding resolution was passed in the European Parliament on 25
October 2018, urging EU countries to impose an EU-wide arms embargo on Saudi Arabia.[352] Germany became the
first Western government to suspend future arms deal with the kingdom after [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Angela_Merkel"] Angela Merkel stated that "arms exports
can't take place in the current circumstances."[353]
According to the new report from the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_Affairs_Canada"] Department of Global Affairs, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canada"] Canada sold record-breaking amount of military
hardware to Saudi Arabia in 2019, despite its poor human rights record.[354]
Human rights
The Saudi government, which mandates Muslim and non-Muslim observance of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sharia"] Sharia law under the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Absolute_monarchy"] absolute rule of
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/House_of_Saud"] House of Saud, have been accused of and denounced by various international organizations and governments for
violating human rights within the country.[355] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Totalitarian"] totalitarian regime ruling the Kingdom of Saudi Arabia is
consistently ranked among the "worstest" in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freedom_House"] Freedom House's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freedom_in_the_World"] annual survey of political and civil rights.[356]
According to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amnesty_International"] Amnesty International, security forces continued to torture and ill- treat detainees to extract confessions
to be used as evidence against them at trial.[357] Saudi Arabia abstained from the United Nations vote adopting the
 Universal Declaration of Human Rights, saying it contradicted [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sharia_law"] sharia law.[358] Mass execution such as those carried
out [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2016_Saudi_Arabia_mass_execution"] in 2016 and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2019_Saudi_Arabia_mass_execution"] in 2019 have been condemned by international rights groups.[359]
Saudi Arabian law does not recognize sexual orientations, religious freedom,
with the public practice of non-Muslim religions is actively prohibited,[362]
and regularly engages in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capital_punishment"] capital punishment, including public executions by
beheading.[363] The death penalty can be imposed for a wide range of
offenses,[364] including murder, rape, armed robbery, repeated drug use,
apostasy,[365] adultery,[236] witchcraft and sorcery[366] and can be carried out
by beheading with a sword,[365] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stoning"] stoning or firing squad,[236] followed by
crucifixion.[366] In April 2020, Saudi Supreme Court issued a directive to
eliminate the punishment of flogging from the Saudi court system, and it is to  [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deera_Square"] Deera Square, central Riyadh. It is a
be replaced by imprisonment or fines.[367][368]  former site of public be-
headings.[360][361]
Saudi women face [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Discrimination"] discrimination in many aspects of their lives, such as the
 justice system, and under the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wali_(Islamic_legal_guardian)"] male guardianship system are effectively treated
as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minor_(law)"] legal minors.[369] Although they make up 70% of those enrolled in universities, for social reasons, women make
up 5% of the workforce in Saudi Arabia,[370] the lowest proportion in the world.The treatment of women has been
referred to as "[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sex_segregation"] sex segregation",[371][372]"gender apartheid".[373][374]
Saudi Arabia is a notable destination country for men and women trafficked for the purposes of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slavery"] slave labour and
commercial sexual exploitation. Men and women from [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Asia"] Central Asia, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_East"] Middle East, and Africa, and many other
countries voluntarily travel to Saudi Arabia as domestic servants or other low-skilled labourers, but some
subsequently face conditions indicative of involuntary servitude.[375]
Geography
Page 19
Saudi Arabia occupies about 80 per cent of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula"] Arabian Peninsula
(the world's largest peninsula),[378] lying between latitudes [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/16th_parallel_north"] 16°
and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/33rd_parallel_north"] 33° N, and longitudes [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/34th_meridian_east"] 34° and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/56th_meridian_east"] 56° E. Because the country's
southern borders with the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates"] United Arab Emirates and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oman"] Oman are not
precisely marked, the exact size of the country is undefined.[378]
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Statistics_Division"] United Nations Statistics Division estimates 2,149,690 km2
(830,000 sq mi) and lists Saudi Arabia as the world's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_area"] 12th largest
state. It is geographically the largest country in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_East"] Middle East
and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabian_Plate"] Arabian Plate.[379]
 Saudi Arabia's diverse geography is dominated by the Arabian
Desert, associated semi-desert, shrubland, steppes, several
mountain ranges, volcanic lava fields and highlands. The
647,500 km2 (250,001 sq mi) [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rub%27_al_Khali"] Rub' al Khali ("Empty Quarter") in
Saudi Arabia topography  the southeastern part of the country is the world's largest
contiguous sand desert.[158][380] Though there are lakes in the
country, Saudi Arabia is the largest country in the world by area
with no permanent rivers. Wadis, non-permanent rivers, however, are very
numerous. The fertile areas are to be found in the alluvial deposits in wadis,
basins, and oases.[158] The main topographical feature is the central plateau
which rises abruptly from the Red Sea and gradually descends into the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nejd"] Nejd
and toward the Persian Gulf. On the Red Sea coast, there is a narrow coastal
plain, known as the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tihamah"] Tihamah parallel to which runs an imposing escarpment.
 Harrat Khaybar seen from the
 International Space Station. Saudi
Arabia is home to more than 2000
dormant volcanoes.[376] Lava fields
in Hejaz, known locally by their
Arabic name of harrat (the singular is 
The southwest province of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%27Asir_Province"] Asir is mountainous, and contains the 3,133 m
(10,279 ft) [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jabal_Sawda"] Mount Sawda, which is the highest point in the country.[158]
Saudi Arabia is home to more than 2000 dormant volcanoes.[376] Lava fields
in Hejaz, known locally by their Arabic name of harrat (the singular is
harrah),  form one of Earth's largest [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alkali_basalt"] alkali basalt regions, covering some
180,000 square kilometres (69,000 sq mi), an area greater than the state of
Missouri.[377]

180,000 square kilometres
(69,000 sq mi), an area greater than
the state of Missouri.[377] 
 Except for the southwestern regions such as Asir, Saudi Arabia has a desert
climate with very high day-time temperatures during the summer and a sharp
temperature drop at night. Average summer temperatures are around 45 °C
(113 °F), but can be as high as 54 °C (129 °F) at its most extreme. In the
winter the temperature rarely drops below 0 °C (32 °F) with the exception of
mostly the northern regions of the country where annual snowfall, in
particular in the mountainous regions of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tabuk_province"] Tabuk province, is not uncommon.[381] The lowest recorded temperature to
date, −12.0 °C (10.4 °F), was measured in Turaif.[382]
In the spring and autumn the heat is temperate, temperatures average around 29 °C (84 °F). Annual rainfall is very
low. The Southern regions differ in that they are influenced by the Indian Ocean monsoons, usually occurring
between October and March. An average of 300 mm (12 in) of rainfall occurs during this period, which is about 60
per cent of the annual precipitation.[383] Saudi Arabia is home to approximately 1300 islands.[384]
Biodiversity
 Saudi Arabia is home to five terrestrial ecoregions: Arabian Peninsula coastal fog desert, Southwestern Arabian
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Sea_Nubo-Sindian_tropical_desert_and_semi-desert"] foothills savanna, Southwestern Arabian montane woodlands, Arabian Desert, and Red Sea Nubo-Sindian tropical
desert and semi-desert.[385]Wildlife includes the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabian_leopard"] Arabian leopard,[386][387] wolf, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Striped_hyena"] striped hyena, mongoose, baboon,
hare, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sand_cat"] sand cat, and jerboa. Animals such as gazelles, oryx, leopards and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asiatic_cheetah"] cheetahs[388] were relatively numerous until
 the 19th century, when extensive hunting reduced these animals almost to extinction. The culturally important Asiatic
lion occurred in Saudi Arabia until the late 19th century before it was hunted to extinction in the wild.[389] Birds
include falcons (which are caught and trained for hunting), eagles, hawks, vultures, sandgrouse, and bulbuls. There
are several species of snakes, many of which are venomous. Saudi Arabia is home to a rich marine life. The Red Sea
Page 20
in particular is a rich and diverse ecosystem. More than [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fish_of_the_Red_Sea"] 1200 species of fish[390]
have been recorded in the Red Sea, and around 10 per cent of these are found
nowhere else.[391] This also includes 42 species of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_deep_water_fish_of_the_Red_Sea"] deepwater fish.[390]
The rich diversity is in part due to the 2,000 km (1,240 mi) of coral reef
extending along its coastline; these [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fringing_reef"] fringing reefs are 5000–7000 years old and
are largely formed of stony [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Acropora"] acropora and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Porites"] porites corals. The reefs form platforms
and sometimes lagoons along the coast and occasional other features such as
cylinders (such as the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blue_Hole_(Red_Sea)"] Blue Hole (Red Sea) at Dahab). These coastal reefs are
 also visited by pelagic species of Red Sea fish, including some of the 44 species
of shark.The Red Sea also contains many offshore reefs including several true
atolls. Many of the unusual offshore reef formations defy classic (i.e.,
Darwinian) coral reef classification schemes, and are generally attributed to the
high levels of tectonic activity that characterize the area.Domesticated animals
include the legendary [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabian_horse"] Arabian horse, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabian_camel"] Arabian camel, sheep, goats, cows,
donkeys, chickens, etc. Reflecting the country's dominant desert conditions,
Saudi Arabia's plant life mostly consists of herbs, plants, and shrubs that require
little water. The date palm (Phoenix dactylifera) is widespread.[158]

13 regional capitals, which have a different status as municipalities (Arabic: ‎أمانة; amanah) headed by mayors
(Arabic: ‎أمين; amin). The governorates are further subdivided into sub-governorates (Arabic: ‎مراكز; [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Markaz_(country_subdivision)"] marakiz, sing.
‎مركز; markaz).

Economy
As of October 2018, Saudi Arabia is the largest economy in the Middle East and the 18th largest in the world.[13]
 Saudi Arabia has the world's second-largest proven petroleum reserves and the country is the largest exporter of
 petroleum.[393][394] It also has the fifth-largest proven natural gas reserves. Saudi Arabia is considered an "energy
superpower".[395][396] It has the second highest total estimated value of natural resources, valued at US$34.4 trillion
in 2016.[397]Saudi Arabia's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Command_economy"] command economy is petroleum-based; roughly 63%[398] of budget revenues and
67%[399] of export earnings come from the oil industry. It is strongly dependent on foreign workers with about 80%
of those employed in the private sector being non-Saudi.[400][401]Challenges to the Saudi economy include halting
Page 21
or reversing the decline in per-capita income, improving education to
prepare youth for the workforce and providing them with employment,
diversifying the economy, stimulating the private sector and housing
construction, and diminishing corruption and inequality.[402]
The oil industry constitutes about 45% of Saudi Arabia's nominal gross
domestic product, compared with 40% from the private sector (see
below).  Saudi Arabia officially has about 260 billion barrels
(4.1×1010 m3) of oil reserves, comprising about one-fifth of the
world's proven total petroleum reserves.[403] 
A proportional representation of Saudi
In the 1990s, Saudi Arabia experienced a significant contraction of oil Arabia exports, 2019
revenues combined with a high rate of population growth. Per capita
income fell from a high of $11,700 at the height of the oil boom in
1981 to $6,300 in 1998.[404] Taking into account the impact of the real oil price changes on the Kingdom's real gross
domestic income, the real command-basis GDP was computed to be 330.381 billion 1999 USD in 2010.[405]
 Increases in oil prices in the early 2000s helped boost per capita GDP to $17,000 in 2007 dollars (about $7,400
adjusted for inflation),[406] but have declined since oil price drop in mid-2014.[407]
 OPEC (the Organization of Petroleum Exporting Countries) limits its
members' oil production based on their "proven reserves." Saudi Arabia's
published reserves have shown little change since 1980, with the main
exception being an increase of about 100 billion barrels (1.6×1010 m3)
between 1987 and 1988.[408] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Matthew_Simmons"] Matthew Simmons has suggested that Saudi
Arabia is greatly exaggerating its reserves and may soon show production
declines (see [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peak_oil"] peak oil).[409]
Office of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi_Aramco"] Saudi Aramco, the world's
most valuable company and the
main source of revenue for the state 
From 2003 to 2013, "several key services" were privatized—municipal water
supply, electricity, telecommunications—and parts of education and health
care, traffic control and car accident reporting were also privatized.
According to Arab News columnist Abdel Aziz Aluwaisheg, "in almost
every one of these areas, consumers have raised serious concerns about the
performance of these privatized entities."[410] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tadawul"] Tadawul All Share Index (TASI) of the Saudi stock exchange
peaked at 16,712.64 in 2005, and closed at 8,535.60, at the end of 2013.[411] In November 2005, Saudi Arabia was
approved as a member of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Trade_Organization"] World Trade Organization. Negotiations to join had focused on the degree to which
 Saudi Arabia is willing to increase market access to foreign goods and in 2000, the government established the Saudi
Arabian General Investment Authority to encourage foreign direct investment in the kingdom. Saudi Arabia
maintains a list of sectors in which foreign investment is prohibited, but the government plans to open some closed
sectors such as telecommunications, insurance, and power transmission/distribution over time. The government has
also made an attempt at "Saudizing" the economy, replacing foreign workers with Saudi nationals with limited
success.[412]
In addition to petroleum and gas, Saudi also has a significant gold mining sector in the ancient [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mahd_adh_Dhahab"] Mahd adh Dhahab
region and significant other mineral industries, an agricultural sector (especially in the southwest but not only) based
on vegetables, fruits, dates etc. and livestock, and large number of temporary jobs created by the roughly two million
annual [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hajj"] hajj pilgrims.[402]Saudi Arabia has had five-year "Development Plans" since 1970. Among its plans were to
launch "economic cities" (e.g. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/King_Abdullah_Economic_City"] King Abdullah Economic City) to be completed by 2020, in an effort to diversify the
economy and provide jobs. As of 2013 four cities were planned.[414] The King has announced that the per capita
income is forecast to rise from $15,000 in 2006 to $33,500 in 2020.[415] The cities will be spread around Saudi
Arabia to promote diversification for each region and their economy, and the cities are projected to contribute $150
billion to the GDP.
Saudi Arabia is increasingly activating its ports in order to participate in trade between Europe and China in addition
to oil transport. To this end, ports such as Jeddah Islamic Port or King Abdullah Economic City are being rapidly
expanded and investments are being made in logistics. The country is historically and currently part of the Maritime
Silk Road that runs from the Chinese coast to the south via the southern tip of India to Mombasa, from there through
Page 22
the Red Sea via the Suez Canal to the Mediterranean, there to the Upper Adriatic
 region to the northern Italian hub of Trieste with its rail connections to Central
Europe, Eastern Europe and the North Sea.[416][417][418][419]
Statistics on poverty in the kingdom are not available through the UN resources
because the Saudi government does not issue any.[420] The Saudi state
discourages calling attention to or complaining about poverty. In December
2011, the Saudi interior ministry arrested three reporters and held them for almost
two weeks for questioning after they uploaded a video on the topic to
YouTube.[421][422][423] Authors of the video claim that 22 per cent of Saudis
may be considered poor (2009).[424] Observers researching the issue prefer to
stay anonymous[425] because of the risk of being arrested.
In September 2018, the Public Investment Fund completed a deal with a group
of global lenders for a loan of $11 billion.[426] The deal raised more than initially
planned and was the first time the PIF had incorporated loans and debt
instruments into its funding.[427] According to data from Fitch Ratings, over two
years starting from May 2016 Saudi Arabia went from having zero debt to
raising $68 billion in dollar-denominated bonds and syndicated loans—one of
the fastest rates among emerging economies.[428] 
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hajj"] hajj is an annual [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam"] Islamic
 pilgrimage to Mecca, the holiest
city for Muslims.[413]
Each year, about a quarter-million young Saudis enter the job market. With
the first phase of Saudization into effect, 70% of sales jobs are expected to be
filled by Saudis. However, the private sector still remains hugely dominated
by foreigners. The rate of local unemployment is 12.9%, its highest in more
than a decade.[427] According to a report published by Bloomberg
Economics in 2018, the government needs to produce 700,000 jobs by 2020
to meet its 9% unemployment target.[427]
The unexpected impact of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic"] COVID-19 pandemic on the economy, along with
Saudi Arabia's poor human rights records, laid unforeseen challenges before
the development plans of the Kingdom, where some of the programs under
 'Vision 2030' were also expected to be affected.[429] On 2 May, the Finance 
King Abdullah Financial Center is
one of the largest investment centres
in the Middle East, located in Riyadh
Minister of Saudi Arabia admitted that the country's economy was facing a
severe economical crisis for the first time in decades, due to the pandemic as well as declining global oil markets.
 Mohammed Al-Jadaan said that the country will take "painful" measures and keep all options open to deal with the
impact.[430]
Agriculture
Serious large-scale agricultural development began in the 1970s. The
government launched an extensive program to promote modern farming
technology; to establish rural roads, irrigation networks and storage and
export facilities; and to encourage agricultural research and training
institutions.As a result, there has been a phenomenal growth in the
production of all basic foods. Saudi Arabia is now completely self-sufficient
in a number of foodstuffs, including meat, milk, and eggs.The country
exports wheat, dates, dairy products, eggs, fish, poultry, fruits, vegetables,
and flowers to markets around the world. Dates, once a staple of the Saudi
diet, are now mainly grown for global humanitarian aid.In addition, Saudi
farmers grow substantial amounts of other grains such as barley, sorghum,
and millet. As of 2016, in the interest of preserving precious water resources,
domestic production of wheat has ended.[431] 
 Al-Hasa is known for its palm trees
and dates. Al-Hasa has over 30
million palm trees which produce
over 100 thousand tons of dates
every year.
Page 23
The Kingdom likewise has some of the most modern and largest dairy farms in the Middle East. Milk production
boasts a remarkably productive annual rate of 6,800 litres (1,800 US gallons) per cow, one of the highest in the
world. The local dairy manufacturing company [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Almarai"] Almarai is the largest vertically integrated dairy company in the
Middle East.[432]
The Kingdom's most dramatic agricultural accomplishment, noted worldwide, was its rapid transformation from
importer to exporter of wheat. In 1978, the country built its first grain silos. By 1984, it had become self-sufficient in
wheat. Shortly thereafter, Saudi Arabia began exporting wheat to some 30 countries, including China and the former
Soviet Union, and in the major producing areas of Tabuk, Hail, and Qasim, average yields reached 8.1 tonnes per
hectare (3.6 short ton/acre).The Kingdom has, however, stepped up fruit and vegetable production, by improving
both agricultural techniques and the roads that link farmers with urban consumers. Saudi Arabia is a major exporter of
fruits and vegetables to its neighbours. Among its most productive crops are watermelon, grapes, citrus fruits, onions,
squash, and tomatoes. At Jizan in the country's well-watered southwest, the Al-Hikmah Research Station is
producing tropical fruits including pineapples, paw-paws, bananas, mangoes, and guavas.[433]
The olive tree is indigenous to Saudi Arabia. In 2018, the Al Jouf Agricultural Development Company received a
certificate of merit from [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Guinness_World_Records"] The Guinness World Records for the largest modern olive plantation in the world. The farm
covers 7730 hectares and has 5 million olive trees. Also, the Guinness World Records took their production capacity
of 15000 tonnes of high-quality olive oil into consideration, while the kingdom consumes double that.The Al Jouf
farms are located in Sakaka, a city in the north-western part of Saudi Arabia, which is a deeply-rooted in history.
Sakaka dates back more than 4,000 years.[434] The Al Jouf region has millions of olive trees and the expected
number is expected to go up to 20 million trees soon.[435] Consuming non-renewable groundwater resulted in the loss
of an estimated four-fifths of the total groundwater reserves by 2012.[436]
Water supply and sanitation
 Water supply and sanitation in Saudi Arabia is characterized by challenges and achievements. One of the main
challenges is [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Water_scarcity"] water scarcity. In order to overcome water scarcity, substantial investments have been undertaken in
 seawater desalination, water distribution, sewerage and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wastewater_treatment"] wastewater treatment. Today about 50% of drinking water
comes from desalination, 40% from the mining of non-renewable groundwater and only 10% from surface water in
the mountainous southwest of the country.[437] Saudi Arabia is suffering from a major depletion of the water in its
underground aquifers and a resultant break down and disintegration of its agriculture as a consequence.[438][439] As a
result of the catastrophe, Saudi Arabia has bought agricultural land in the United States,[440][441] Argentina,[442] and
Africa.[443][444][445][446] Saudi Arabia ranked as a major buyer of agricultural land in foreign countries.[447][448]
According to the Joint Monitoring Program (JMP) for Water Supply and Sanitation of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WHO"] WHO and UNICEF, the
latest reliable source on access to water and sanitation in Saudi Arabia is the 2004 census. It indicates that 97% of the
population had access to an improved source of drinking water and 99% had access to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Improved_sanitation"] improved sanitation. For 2015,
the JMP estimates that access to sanitation increased to 100%. Sanitation was primarily through on-site solutions and
only about 40% of the population was connected to sewers.[449] In 2015, still 886 thousand people lacked access to
"improved" water.[450][451]
Tourism
Although most tourism in Saudi Arabia still largely involves religious pilgrimages, there is growth in the leisure
tourism sector. According to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Bank"] World Bank, approximately 14.3 million people visited Saudi Arabia in 2012,
making it the world's 19th-most-visited country.[452] Tourism is an important component of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi_Vision_2030"] Saudi Vision 2030
and according to a report conducted by BMI Research in 2018, both religious and non-religious tourism have
significant potential for expansion.[453]
Starting December 2018, the kingdom offers an electronic visa for foreign visitors to attend sports events and
concerts. The "sharek" visa process started on 15 December 2018 when the Saudi Ad Diriyah E Prix race
started.[454] In September 2019, the Kingdom announced its plans to open visa applications for visitors, where people
from about 50 countries would be able to get tourist visas to Saudi.[455] In January 2020, it was announced that
holders of a US, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Kingdom"] UK or [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Schengen_Area"] Schengen visa are eligible for a Saudi electronic visa upon arrival.[456]

Demographics
The population of Saudi Arabia as of July 2013 is estimated to be 26.9
million, including between 5.5 million[5] and 10 million non-nationalized
immigrants,[401][457] though the Saudi population has long proved difficult to
accurately estimate due to Saudi leaders' historical tendency to inflate census
results.[458] Saudi population has grown rapidly since 1950 when it was
estimated to be 3 million,[459] and for many years had one of the highest
population growth rates in the world at around 3 per cent a year.[460]
 The ethnic composition of Saudi citizens is 90% Arab and 10% Afro-
Arab.[461] Most Saudis live in the Hejaz (35%), Najd (28%), and the Eastern
Province (15%).[462] Hejaz is the most populated region in Saudi Arabia.[463]
As late as 1970, most Saudis lived a subsistence life in the rural provinces,
but in the last half of the 20th century, the kingdom has urbanized rapidly. As
of 2012 about 80% of Saudis live in urban metropolitan areas—specifically
Riyadh, Jeddah, or Dammam.[464][465] 
Saudi Arabia population density
(people per km2)
Its population is also quite young with over half the population under 25 years old.[466] A large fraction are foreign
nationals. (The CIA Factbook estimated that as of 2013 foreign nationals living in Saudi Arabia made up about 21%
of the population.[5] Other estimates are 30%[467] or 33%[468]) Immigrants make up 38.3% of the total population,
according to UN data (2019), mostly coming from the Middle East, Asia, and Africa.[469] As recently as the early
1960s, Saudi Arabia's slave population was estimated at 300,000.[470] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_slavery_in_the_Muslim_world"] Slavery was officially abolished in
1962.[471][472]
