Languages
The official language of Saudi Arabia is Arabic. The three main regional variants spoken by Saudis are [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Najdi_Arabic"] Najdi Arabic
(about 14.6 million speakers[483]), [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hejazi_Arabic"] Hejazi Arabic (about 10.3 million speakers[484]), and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_Arabic"] Gulf Arabic (about 0.96
million speakers[485]). [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Faifi_language"] Faifi is spoken by about 50,000. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi_Sign_Language"] Saudi Sign Language is the principal language of the deaf
community, amounting to around 100,000 speakers. The large expatriate communities also speak their own
languages, the most numerous of which, according to 2018 data, are [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bengali_language"] Bengali (~1,500,000), [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tagalog_language"] Tagalog (~900,000),
 Eastern Punjabi (~800,000), [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Urdu"] Urdu (~740,000), [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egyptian_Arabic"] Egyptian Arabic (~600,000), Rohingya, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Levantine_Arabic"] North Levantine Arabic
(both ~500,000)[486] and Malayalam.[487]
Religions
Virtually all Saudi citizens are Muslim[488] (officially, all are), and almost all Saudi residents are Muslim.[489][490]
Estimates of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sunni"] Sunni population of Saudi Arabia range between 75% and 90%, with the remaining 10–25% being
 Shia Muslim.[491][492][493][494][495] The official and dominant form of Sunni Islam in Saudi Arabia is commonly
known as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wahhabism"] Wahhabism[496] (proponents prefer the name Salafism, considering Wahhabi derogatory[497]), which was
founded in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula"] Arabian Peninsula by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhammad_ibn_Abd_al-Wahhab"] Muhammad ibn Abd al-Wahhab in the 18th century. Other denominations, such
as the minority [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia_Islam"] Shia Islam, are systematically suppressed.[498]
According to estimates there are about 1,500,000 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christianity_in_Saudi_Arabia"] Christians in Saudi Arabia, almost all foreign workers.[499] Saudi
Arabia allows Christians to enter the country as foreign workers for temporary work, but does not allow them to
practice their faith openly. The percentage of Saudi Arabian citizens who are Christians is officially zero,[500] as
Saudi Arabia forbids religious conversion from Islam (apostasy) and punishes it by death.[501] According to Pew
Research Center there are 390,000 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hindus"] Hindus in Saudi Arabia, almost all foreign workers.[502] There may be a
significant fraction of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atheism"] atheists and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agnosticism"] agnostics in Saudi Arabia,[503][504] although they are officially called
"terrorists".[505] In its 2017 religious freedom report, the US State Department named Saudi Arabia a Country of
Particular Concern (CPC).[506]
Education
Education is free at all levels, although higher education is restricted to citizens only.[507] The school system is
composed of elementary, intermediate, and secondary schools. Classes are segregated by sex. At secondary level,
students are able to choose from 3 types of schools: general education, vocational and technical, or religious.[508] The
Page 26
rate of literacy is 97.1% among males and is about 92.71% among females
(2017).[509] For the youth, literacy rate rose up to 99.55% among males and
99.45% among females (2020).[510][511]
According to the educational plan for secondary (high school) education
1435–1438 Hijri, students enrolling in the "natural sciences" path are required
to take five religion subjects which are: Tawhid, Fiqh, Tafseer, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hadith"] Hadith and
 Islamic Education and Quran. However, in 2021 the Saudi Ministry of
Education merged the multiple Islamic subjects into one single book as part of
a series of reforms to revamp the school education system.[512] In addition,
students are required to take six science subjects which are Maths, Physics,
Chemistry, Biology, Geology and Computer.[513] 
Laboratory buildings at [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/KAUST"] KAUST
 Higher education has expanded rapidly, with large numbers of universities
and colleges being founded particularly since 2000. Institutions of higher
education include the country's first university, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/King_Saud_University"] King Saud University founded
 in 1957, the Islamic University at Medina founded in 1961, and the King
Abdulaziz University in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jeddah"] Jeddah founded in 1967. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Princess_Nora_bint_Abdul_Rahman_University"] Princess Norah University,
 the largest women's university in the world, was founded in 1970. King
Abdullah University of Science and Technology, known as KAUST,
founded recently in 2009. Other colleges and universities emphasize curricula
in sciences and technology, military studies, religion, and medicine. Institutes
devoted to Islamic studies, in particular, abound. Women typically receive
college instruction in segregated institutions.[158] 
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Yamamah_Private_University"] Al-Yamamah Private University
in Riyadh
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities"] Academic Ranking of World Universities, known as Shanghai Ranking,
ranked 4 Saudi institutions among its 2021 list of the 500 top universities in
the world.[514] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings"] QS World University Rankings lists 14 Saudi universities
among the 2022 world’s top universities and 23 universities among the top
 100 in the Arab world.[515] The 2022 list of U.S. News & World Report Best
Global University Ranking ranked King Abdulaziz University among the top
50 universities in the world and King Abdullah University of Science and
Technology among the top 100 universities in the world.
In 2018, Saudi Arabia ranked 28th worldwide in terms of high-quality
research output according to the scientific journal Nature.[516]This makes
Saudi Arabia the best performing Middle Eastern, Arab, and Muslim country. 
 UIS literacy rate Saudi Arabia
population, 15 plus, 1990–2015
Saudi Arabia spends 8.8% of its gross domestic product on education,
compared with the global average of 4.6%.[517] Saudi Arabia was ranked
66th in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_Innovation_Index"] Global Innovation Index in 2021, up from 68th in 2019.[518][519][520][521]
Memorization by rote of large parts of the Qur'an, its interpretation and understanding (Tafsir) and the application of
Islamic tradition to everyday life is at the core of the curriculum. Religion taught in this manner is also a compulsory
subject for all University students.[522] As a consequence, Saudi youth "generally lacks the education and technical
skills the private sector needs" according to the CIA.[5] Similarly, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Chronicle_of_Higher_Education"] The Chronicle of Higher Education wrote in 2010
that "the country needs educated young Saudis with marketable skills and a capacity for innovation and
entrepreneurship. That's not generally what Saudi Arabia's educational system delivers, steeped as it is in rote learning
and religious instruction."[523]
The religious sector of the Saudi national curriculum was examined in a 2006 report by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freedom_House"] Freedom House which
concluded that "the Saudi public school religious curriculum continues to propagate an ideology of hate toward the
'unbeliever', that is, Christians, Jews, Shiites, Sufis, Sunni Muslims who do not follow Wahhabi doctrine, Hindus,
atheists and others".[524][525] The Saudi religious studies curriculum is taught outside the Kingdom via Saudi-linked
madrasah, schools, and clubs throughout the world.[526] Critics have described the education system as "medieval"
and that its primary goal "is to maintain the rule of absolute monarchy by casting it as the ordained protector of the
faith, and that Islam is at war with other faiths and cultures".[527] This radical teaching takes place in Saudi funded
mosques and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Madrasas"] madrasas across the Islamic world from Morocco to Pakistan to Indonesia.[528]
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fiqh"]
Page 27
The approach taken in the Saudi education system has been accused of encouraging [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_terrorism"] Islamic terrorism, leading to
reform efforts.[529][530] Following the 9/11 attacks, the government aimed to tackle the twin problems of encouraging
extremism and the inadequacy of the country's university education for a modern economy, by slowly modernising
the education system through the "Tatweer" reform program.[529] The Tatweer program is reported to have a budget
of approximately US$2 billion and focuses on moving teaching away from the traditional Saudi methods of
memorization and rote learning towards encouraging students to analyse and problem-solve. It also aims to create an
education system which will provide a more secular and vocationally based training.[523][531]
In 2021, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Washington_Post"] Washington Post newspaper published a report on the measures taken by Saudi Arabia to clean
textbooks from paragraphs considered anti-Semitic and anti-women. The paragraphs dealing with the punishment of
homosexuality or same-sex relations have been deleted, and expressions of admiration for the extremist martyrdom.
Anti-Semitic expressions and calls to fight the Jews became fewer. David Weinberg, director of international affairs
for the Anti-Defamation League in Washington, said that references to demonizing Jews, Christians, and Shiites have
been removed from some places or have toned down, noting the deletion of paragraphs that talk about killing gays,
infidels and witches. The US State Department expressed in an email that it welcomed the changes to the materials
affecting Saudi educational curricula. The Foreign Ministry supports a training program for Saudi teachers.[532]
Health care
Health care in Saudi Arabia is a national health care system in which the
government provides free health care services through a number of
government agencies. Saudi Arabia has been ranked among the 26 best
 countries in providing high quality healthcare.[533] The Saudi Ministry of
Health (MOH) is the major [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Government"] government agency entrusted with the provision
of preventive, curative, and rehabilitative health care for the Kingdom's
population.The Ministry's origins can be traced to 1925, when a number of
regional health departments were established, with the first in Makkah, Saudi
Arabia.The various healthcare institutions were merged to become a
ministerial body in 1950.[534] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abdullah_bin_Faisal_Al_Saud"] Abdullah bin Faisal Al Saud was the first
health minister and served in the position for three years, with his main role to
set up the newly formed Ministry.[535] 
Historical development of life
expectancy in Saudi Arabia
The Health Ministry created a friendly [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Competition"] competition between each of the districts, and between different medical
services and hospitals. This idea resulted in the creation of the "Ada'a" project launched in 2016. The new system is a
nationwide performance indicator, for services and hospitals. Following the implementation of the new KPI tables,
waiting times and other major measurements improved dramatically across the Kingdom.[536]
A new strategy has been developed by the Ministry, known as Diet and Physical Activity Strategy or DPAS for
short.[537] Many lifestyle issues in the country were causing bad lifestyle choices. This led to the Ministry advising
that there should be a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tax"] tax increase on unhealthy food, drink and also cigarettes in the region. This additional tax could
be utilized to improve healthcare offerings. The tax was implemented in 2017.[538] As part of the same strategy,
calorie labels were added in 2019 to a number of food and drink products. Ingredients were also listed, not as an aim
to reduce obesity, but also for citizens with health issues, to manage their diet.[539] As part of the ongoing focus on
tackling obesity, women-only gyms were allowed to open in 2017. A number of sports were offered in each of these
 gyms, including bodybuilding, running and swimming to maintain higher standards of health.[540][541]Smoking in
Saudi-Arabia in all age groups was widespread. In 2009 the lowest median percentage of smokers was university
students (~13.5%) while the highest was elderly people (~25%). The study also found the median percentage of male
smokers to be much higher than that of females (~26.5% for males, ~9% for females). Before 2010, Saudi Arabia had
no policies banning or restricting smoking.
The MOH has been awarded "Healthy City" certificates by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Health_Organization"] World Health Organization (WHO) for the cities of
 Unayzah and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Riyadh_Al_Khabra"] Riyadh Al Khabra as 4th and 5th Healthy Cities in Saudi Arabia.[542]The WHO had earlier classified
three Saudi Arabian cities, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ad_Diriyah"] Ad Diriyah, Jalajil, and Al-Jamoom as "Healthy city", as part of the WHO Healthy Cities
Program. Recently [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Baha"] Al-Baha has also been classified as a healthy city to join the list of global healthy cities approved
by the World Health Organization.[543]
Page 28
In May 2019, the then Saudi Minister of Health [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tawfig_AlRabiah"] Dr. Tawfiq bin Fawzan AlRabiah received a global award on behalf
of the Kingdom for combatting smoking through social awareness, treatment, and application of regulations.[544] The
award was presented as part of the 72nd session of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Health_Assembly"] World Health Assembly, held in Geneva in May 2019. After
becoming one of the first nations to ratify the WHO Framework Convention on Tobacco Control in 2005, it plans to
reduce tobacco use from 12.7% in 2017, to 5% in 2030.[544]
Saudi Arabia has a life expectancy of 74.99 years (73.79 for males and 76.61 for females) according to the latest data
for the year 2018 from the World Bank.[545] Infant mortality in 2019 was 5.7 per 1,000.[545] In 2016, 69.7% of the
adult population was overweight and 35.5% was obese.[546]
Foreigners
Saudi Arabia's Central Department of Statistics & Information estimated the foreign population at the end of 2014 at
33% (10.1 million).[547] The CIA Factbook estimated that as of 2013 foreign nationals living in Saudi Arabia made
up about 21% of the population.[5] Other sources report differing estimates.[468] Indian: 1.5 million, Pakistani: 1.3
million,[548] Egyptian: 900,000, Yemeni: 800,000, Bangladeshi: 400,000, Filipino: 500,000, Jordanian/Palestinian:
260,000, Indonesian: 250,000, Sri Lankan: 350,000, Sudanese: 250,000, Syrian: 100,000 and Turkish: 80,000.[549]
According to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Guardian"] The Guardian, as of 2013 there were more than half a million [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Migrant_domestic_workers"] foreign-born domestic workers in Saudi
Arabia. Most have backgrounds in poverty and come from Africa, the Indian subcontinent and Southeast Asia.[550]
To go to work in Saudi Arabia, they must often pay large sums to recruitment agencies in their home countries. The
agencies then handle the necessary legal paperwork.[551]As the Saudi population grows and oil export revenues
stagnate, pressure for "Saudization" (the replacement of foreign workers with Saudis) has grown, and the Saudi
government hopes to decrease the number of foreign nationals in the country.[552] Saudi Arabia expelled 800,000
Yemenis in 1990 and 1991[553] and has built a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi%E2%80%93Yemen_barrier"] Saudi–Yemen barrier against an influx of illegal immigrants and
against the smuggling of drugs and weapons.[554] In November 2013, Saudi Arabia expelled thousands of illegal
Ethiopian residents from the Kingdom. Various Human Rights entities have criticized Saudi Arabia's handling of the
issue.[555] Over 500,000 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Illegal_immigration_in_Saudi_Arabia"] undocumented migrant workers — mostly from Somalia, Ethiopia, and Yemen — have
been detained and deported since 2013.[556] An investigation led by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Sunday_Telegraph"] The Sunday Telegraph, exposed the condition of
African migrants who were detained in Saudi Arabia allegedly for containing [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coronavirus_disease_2019"] COVID-19 in the kingdom. They were
beaten, tortured, and electrocuted. Many of the migrants died due to heatstroke or by attempting suicide, after being
severely beaten and tortured. The migrants lack proper living conditions, provision of food and water.[557]
Foreigners cannot apply for [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Permanent_residency"] permanent residency, though a specialized [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Premium_Residency"] Premium Residency visa became available in
2019.[558] Only Muslims can become Saudi citizens.[559] Foreigners who have resided in the kingdom and hold
degrees in various scientific fields may apply for Saudi citizenship,[560][561] and exception made for Palestinians who
are excluded unless married to a male Saudi national, because of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_League"] Arab League instructions barring the Arab states
from granting them citizenship. Saudi Arabia is not a signatory to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Convention_relating_to_the_Status_of_Refugees"] 1951 UN Refugee Convention.[562]
Culture
Saudi Arabia has centuries-old attitudes and traditions, often derived from Arab civilization. The main factors that
influence the culture of Saudi Arabia are Islamic heritage and Bedouin traditions as well as its historical role as an
ancient trade centre.[563]
Religion in society
Religion is a core aspect of everyday life in Saudi Arabia. It plays a dominant role in the country's governance and
legal system, deeply influences culture and daily life, although the power of the religious establishment has been
significantly eroded in the 2010s.[23] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hejaz"] Hejaz region, where the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holiest_sites_in_Islam"] Islamic holy cities of Mecca and Medina are
located, is the destination of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hajj"] Ḥajj pilgrimage, and often deemed to be the cradle of Islam.[564][e]
Page 29
Islam is the state religion of Saudi Arabia. There is no law that requires all
citizens to be Muslim, but non-Muslims and many foreign and Saudi Muslims
whose beliefs are deemed not to conform with the government's interpretation
of Islam must practice their religion in private and are vulnerable to
discrimination, harassment, detention, and, for foreigners, deportation.[575]
 Neither Saudi citizens nor guest workers have the right of freedom of
religion.[576] The dominant form of Islam in the kingdom—Wahhabism—
arose in the central region of Najd, in the 18th century. Proponents call the
movement "Salafism",[497] and believe that its teachings purify the practice of
Islam of innovations or practices that deviate from the seventh-century
teachings of Muhammad and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sahaba"] his companions.[577] The Saudi government
has often been viewed as an active oppressor of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia_Islam"] Shia Muslims because of the
funding of the Wahhabi ideology which denounces the Shia faith.[578][579]
Prince [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bandar_bin_Sultan"] Bandar bin Sultan, Saudi ambassador to the United States, stated:
"The time is not far off in the Middle East when it will be literally 'God help
the Shia'. More than a billion Sunnis have simply had enough of them."[580] 
 Supplicating pilgrim at Al-Masjid Al-
Ḥarām (The Sacred Mosque) in
Mecca. The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kaaba"] Kaaba is the cubic
building in front of the pilgrim.
Saudi Arabia is one of the few countries that have "[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Committee_for_the_Promotion_of_Virtue_and_the_Prevention_of_Vice_(Saudi_Arabia)"] religious police" (known as Haia or Mutaween), who patrol the
streets "[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Enjoining_good_and_forbidding_wrong"] enjoining good and forbidding wrong" by enforcing [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clothing_laws_by_country"] dress codes, strict [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sex_segregation"] separation of men and women,
attendance at prayer ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salat"] salat) five times each day, the ban on alcohol, and other aspects of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sharia"] Sharia (Islamic law).
However, since 2016 the power of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Committee_for_the_Promotion_of_Virtue_and_the_Prevention_of_Vice_(Saudi_Arabia)"] religious police was curbed, which barred them from pursuing, questioning,
requesting identification or arresting suspects.[332] In the privacy of homes, behaviour can be far looser, and reports
from [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WikiLeaks"] WikiLeaks indicate that low ranked members of the ruling Saudi Royal family indulge in parties with alcohol,
drugs, and prostitutes.[581]
Until 2016, the kingdom only used the lunar [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_calendar"] Islamic calendar, not the international [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gregorian_calendar"] Gregorian calendar,[582] but in
2016 the kingdom announced its switch to the Gregorian calendar for civil purposes.[583][584] Daily life is influenced
by Islamic observance. Some businesses decide to close three or four times a day[585] for 30 to 45 minutes during
business hours while employees and customers are sent off to pray.[586][587] The weekend is Friday-Saturday, not
Saturday-Sunday because Friday is the holiest day for Muslims.[158][588] For many years only two religious holidays
were publicly recognized – [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%CA%BF%C4%AAd_al-Fi%E1%B9%ADr"] ʿĪd al-Fiṭr and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%CA%BF%C4%AAd_al-A%E1%B8%8D%E1%B8%A5%C4%81"] ʿĪd al-Aḍḥā. (ʿĪd al-Fiṭr is "the biggest" holiday, a three-day period of
"feasting, gift-giving and general letting go").[589]
In 2004, approximately half of the broadcast airtime of Saudi [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Television_in_Saudi_Arabia#State-managed_stations"] state television was devoted to religious issues.[590] 90
per cent of books published in the kingdom were on religious subjects, and most of the doctorates awarded by its
universities were in Islamic studies.[591] In the state school system, about half of the material taught is religious. In
contrast, assigned readings over 12 years of primary and secondary schooling devoted to covering the history,
literature, and cultures of the non-Muslim world come to a total of about 40 pages.[590]
"Fierce religious resistance" had to be overcome to permit such innovations
as paper money (in 1951), female education (1964), and television (1965) and
the abolition of slavery (1962).[592] Public support for the traditional
political/religious structure of the kingdom is so strong that one researcherinterviewing Saudis found virtually no support for reforms to secularize the
state.[593]
Celebration of other (non-Wahhabi) Islamic holidays, such as the
 Muhammad's birthday and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Day_of_Ashura"] Day of Ashura, (an important holiday for the
10–25 per cent of the population[492][493][494] that is [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia"] Shīʿa Muslim), are
tolerated only when celebrated locally and on a small scale.[594] Shias also
face systematic discrimination in employment, education, the justice system
according to Human Rights Watch.[595][596] Non-Muslim festivals like 
Non-Muslims are prohibited from
entering the Islamic holy city of
Mecca
Christmas, Easter, Halloween, and New Year were not tolerated until
recently.[597][598][599] No churches, temples or other non-Muslim houses of worship are permitted in the country.
 Proselytizing by non-Muslims and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apostasy_in_Islam"] conversion by Muslims to another religion is illegal,[600] and as of 2014 the
distribution of "publications that have prejudice to any other religious belief other than Islam" (such as Bibles), was
Page 30
reportedly punishable by death.[601] In legal compensation court cases ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diyya"] Diyya) non-Muslim are awarded less than
Muslims.[602] Atheists are legally designated as terrorists.[603] At least one religious minority, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ahmadiyya"] Ahmadiyya
Muslims, had its adherents deported,[604] as they are legally banned from entering the country.[605]
In a recent move to promote a modern image, Saudi Arabia banned the religious group known as 'Tablighi Jamaat'.
The announcement was made on social media by the country's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ministry_of_Islamic_Affairs"] Minister of Islamic Affairs who warned people against
association during the Friday sermon.[606]
Women in society
Throughout history, women did not have equal rights to men in the kingdom; the
 U.S. State Department considers Saudi Arabian government's discrimination against
women a "significant problem" in Saudi Arabia and notes that women have few
 political rights due to the government's discriminatory policies.[607] The World
Economic Forum 2021 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_Gender_Gap_Report"] Global Gender Gap Report ranked Saudi Arabia 147th out of
156 countries for gender parity.[608] However, since [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohammed_bin_Salman,_Crown_Prince_of_Saudi_Arabia"] Mohammed bin Salman was
appointed [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crown_Prince_of_Saudi_Arabia"] Crown Prince in 2017, a series of social reforms have been witnessed
regarding women's rights.
Under Saudi law, every adult female must have a male relative as her "guardian"
([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wali_(Islamic_legal_guardian)"] wali),[607] As of 2008, a woman was required to have permission from her male
guardian in order to travel, study, or work.[607][609] A royal decree passed in May
2017 allowed them to avail government services such as education and healthcare
without the need of a consent of a male guardian. The order however also stated that
it should only be allowed if it does not contradict the Sharia system.[610][611]
According to a leading Saudi feminist and journalist, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wajeha_al-Huwaider"] Wajeha al-Huwaider, "Saudi
women are weak, no matter how high their status, even the 'pampered' ones among
them, because they have no law to protect them from attack by anyone."[612]
Women face discrimination in the courts, where the testimony of one man equals that
of two women [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Legal_system_of_Saudi_Arabia#Family_law"] in family and inheritance law.[607] Polygamy is permitted for
men,[613] and men have a unilateral right to divorce their wives (talaq) without
needing any legal justification.[614] A woman can only obtain a divorce with the
consent of her husband or judicially if her husband has harmed her.[615] In practice, it
is very difficult for a Saudi woman to obtain a judicial divorce.[615] With regard to the
law of inheritance, the Quran specifies that fixed portions of the deceased's estate
must be left to the Qur'anic heirs[616] and generally, female heirs receive half the
portion of male heirs.[616] 
 Sarah Attar is a track and
field athlete who competed
 at the 2012 Summer
Olympics as one of the first
two female Olympians
representing Saudi Arabia.
Obesity is a problem among middle and upper-class Saudis who have domestic servants to do traditional work but,
until 2018, were forbidden to drive and so are limited in their ability to leave their home.[617] As of April 2014, Saudi
authorities in the education ministry have been asked by the Shoura Council to consider lifting a state school ban on
sports for girls with the proviso that any sports conform to Sharia rules on dress and gender segregation, according to
the official SPA news agency.[401] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_religious_police"] religious police, known as the mutawa, imposed many restrictions on women
in public in Saudi Arabia.[607][618] The restrictions include forcing women to sit in separate specially designated
family sections in restaurants, to wear an [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abaya"] abaya and to cover their hair.[607] However, in 2016, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Consultative_Assembly_of_Saudi_Arabia"] Saudi cabinet has
drastically reduced the power of the religious police and barred it "from pursuing, questioning, asking for
identification, arresting and detaining anyone suspected of a crime".
A few Saudi women have risen to the top of the medical profession; for example, Dr. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adah_Almutairi"] Ghada Al-Mutairi heads a
 medical research centre in California[619] and Dr. Salwa Al-Hazzaa is head of the ophthalmology department at King
Faisal Specialist Hospital in Riyadh and was the late King Fahad's personal ophthalmologist.[620]
Heritage sites
Page 31
Saudi [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wahhabism"] Wahhabism is hostile to any reverence given to historical or religious
places of significance for fear that it may give rise to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shirk_(Islam)"] 'shirk' (idolatry), and the
most significant historic Muslim sites (in Mecca and Medina) are located in
the western Saudi region of the Hejaz.[564] As a consequence, under Saudi
rule, an estimated 95% of Mecca's historic buildings, most over a thousand
years old, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Destruction_of_early_Islamic_heritage_sites_in_Saudi_Arabia"] have been demolished for religious reasons.[621] Critics claim that
over the last 50 years, 300 historic sites linked to Muhammad, his family or
companions have been lost,[622] leaving fewer than 20 structures remaining The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Masjid_al-Haram"] Masjid al-Haram is the holiest
in Mecca that date back to the time of Muhammad.[623] Demolished [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic"] Islamic site, located in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mecca"] Mecca
structures include the mosque originally built by Muhammad's daughter
Fatima, and other mosques founded by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abu_Bakr"] Abu Bakr (Muhammad's father-in-
 law and the first Caliph), Umar (the second Caliph), Ali (Muhammad's son-in-law and the fourth Caliph), and Salman
al-Farsi (another of Muhammad's companions).[624]
Six cultural sites in Saudi Arabia are designated as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Sites"] UNESCO World Heritage Sites: Al-Hijr Archaeological Site
 (Madâin Sâlih);[625] the Turaif district in the city of Diriyah;[626] Historic Jeddah, the Gate to Mecca;[627] Al-Ahsa
Oasis;[628] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rock_Art_in_the_Ha%27il_Region"] Rock Art in the Hail Region;[629] and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bir_Hima_Rock_Petroglyphs_and_Inscriptions"] Ḥimā Cultural Area.[630] Ten other sites submitted requests for
recognition to UNESCO in 2015.[631] 
 There are six elements inscribed on UNESCO's Intangible Cultural Heritage
of Humanity list:[632] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Qatt_Al-Asiri"] Al-Qatt Al-Asiri, female traditional interior wall
decoration in Asir; Almezmar, drumming and dancing with sticks; Falconry,
a living human heritage; [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabic_coffee"] Arabic coffee, a symbol of generosity; Majlis, a
cultural and social space; Alardah Alnajdiyah, dance, drumming and poetry
in Saudi Arabia.
 In June 2014, the Council of Ministers approved a law that gives the Saudi
Commission for Tourism and National Heritage the means to protect Saudi
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mosque_of_the_Prophet"] Mosque of the Prophet in
 Medina containing the tomb of
 Muhammad 
Arabia's ancient relics and historic sites. Within the framework of the 2016
National Transformation Program, also known as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi_Vision_2030"] Saudi Vision 2030, the
kingdom allocated 900 million euros to preserve its historical and cultural
heritage.[633] Saudi Arabia also participates in the International Alliance for
the Protection of Heritage in Conflict Areas (ALIPH), created in March 2017,
with a contribution of 18.5 million euros.[634]
In 2017, Crown Prince Mohammad bin Salman promised to return Saudi Arabia to the "moderate Islam" of the era
before the 1979 Iranian revolution.[635] A new centre, the King Salman Complex for the Prophet's Hadith, was
established that year to monitor interpretations of the Prophet Mohammed's hadiths to prevent them being used to
justifying terrorism.[636]
In March 2018, the Crown Prince met the Archbishop of Canterbury during a visit to the UK, pledging to promote
interfaith dialogue. In Riyadh the following month King Salman met the head of the Vatican's Pontifical Council for
Interreligious Dialogue.[637] In July 2019, UNESCO signed a letter with the Saudi Minister of Culture in which
Saudi Arabia contributed US$25 million to UNESCO for the preservation of heritage.[638]
Dress
Saudi Arabian dress strictly follows the principles of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hijab"] hijab (the Islamic principle of modesty, especially in dress). The
predominantly loose and flowing, but covering, garments are suited to Saudi Arabia's desert climate. Traditionally,
men usually wear a white ankle-length garment woven from wool or cotton (known as a thawb), with a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Keffiyeh"] keffiyeh (a
large checkered square of cotton held in place by an agal) or a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Keffiyeh"] ghutra (a plain white square made of a finer cotton,
also held in place by an agal) worn on the head. For rare chilly days, Saudi men wear a camel-hair cloak (bisht) over
the top. In public women are required to wear a black [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abaya"] abaya or other black clothing that covers everything under the
neck with the exception of their hands and feet, although most women cover their head in respect of their religion.
Page 32
This requirement applies to non-Muslim women too and failure to abide can result in police action, particularly in
more conservative areas of the country. Women's clothes are often decorated with tribal motifs, coins, sequins,
metallic thread, and appliques.
 Ghutrah (Arabic: ‎غتره) is a traditional [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Headdress"] headdress typically worn by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab"] Arab men. It is made of a square of
cloth ("scarf"), usually cotton, folded and wrapped in various styles around the head. It is commonly
worn in areas with an [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arid"] arid climate, to provide protection from direct [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sun_exposure"] sun exposure, and also protection
of the mouth and eyes from blown dust and sand.
 Agal (Arabic: ‎عقال) is an item of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab"] Arab headgear constructed of cord which is fastened around the
 Ghutrah to hold it in place. The agal is usually black in colour.
 Thawb (Arabic: ‎ثوب) is the standard Arabic word for garment. It is ankle-length, usually with long
sleeves, similar to a robe.
 Bisht (Arabic: ‎بشت) is a traditional Arabic men's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cloak"] cloak usually only worn for prestige on special
occasions such as weddings.
 Abaya (Arabic: ‎عبائة) is a woman's garment. It is a black cloak that loosely covers the entire body
except for the head. Some women choose to cover their faces with a niqāb and some do not. Some
abayas cover the top of the head as well.[639]
Arts and entertainment
During the 1970s, cinemas were numerous in the Kingdom although they were seen
as contrary to Wahhabi norms.[640] During the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_revival"] Islamic revival movement in the
1980s, and as a political response to an increase in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamist"] Islamist activism including the
1979 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grand_Mosque_Seizure"] seizure of the Grand Mosque in Mecca, the government closed all cinemas
and theatres. However, with King Abdullah and King Salman's reforms, cinemas
re-opened,[641] including one in KAUST.
From the 18th century onward, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wahhabi"] Wahhabi fundamentalism discouraged artistic
development inconsistent with its teaching. In addition, Sunni Islamic prohibition of
creating representations of people have limited the visual arts, which tend to be
dominated by geometric, floral, and abstract designs and by calligraphy. With the
advent of the oil-wealth in the 20th century came exposure to outside influences,
such as Western housing styles, furnishings, and clothes. Music and dance have
always been part of Saudi life. Traditional music is generally associated with poetry
and is sung collectively. Instruments include the rabābah, an instrument not unlike a 
King Abdullah practising
falconry, a traditional pursuit
in the country
three-string fiddle, and various types of percussion instruments, such as the ṭabl
(drum) and the ṭār (tambourine). Of the native dances, the most popular is a martial
line dance known as the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ardah"] arḍah, which includes lines of men, frequently armed with swords or rifles, dancing to the
beat of drums and tambourines. Bedouin poetry, known as nabaṭī, is still very popular.[158]
Censorship has limited the development of Saudi literature, although several [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Saudi_Arabian_writers"] Saudi novelists and poets have achieved
critical and popular acclaim in the Arab world—albeit generating official hostility in their home country. These
 include Ghazi Algosaibi, Mansour al-Nogaidan, Abdelrahman Munif, Turki al-Hamad and Rajaa al-
Sanea.[642][643][644] In 2016, the General Entertainment Authority was formed to oversee the expansion of the Saudi
entertainment sector.[645]The first concerts in Riyadh for 25 years took place the following year.[646] Other events
since the GEA's creation have included comedy shows, professional wrestling events and monster truck rallies.[647]
In 2018 the first public cinema opened after a ban of 35 years, with plans to have more than 2,000 screens running by
2030.[648]
Developments in the arts in 2018 included Saudi Arabia's debut appearances at the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cannes_Film_Festival"] Cannes Film Festival and the
 Venice Biennale.[649][650] Guetta's comments come as Saudi Arabia increasingly attracts big name western music
acts to perform in the kingdom.[651]
Cuisine
Page 33
 Saudi Arabian cuisine is similar to that of the surrounding countries in the Arabian
Peninsula and the wider Arab world, and has influenced and been influenced by
Turkish, Indian, Persian, and African food. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_dietary_laws"] Islamic dietary laws are enforced: pork is not
allowed and other animals are slaughtered in accordance with halal. Kebabs and falafel
are popular, as is shāwarmā (shawarma), a marinated grilled meat dish of lamb, mutton,
or chicken. As in other Arab countries of the Arabian Peninsula, machbūs (kabsa), a rice
dish with lamb, chicken, fish or shrimp, is among the national dishes as well as the dish
mandi. Flat, unleavened [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taboon_bread"] taboon bread is a staple of virtually every meal, as are dates,
fresh fruit, yoghurt, and hummus. Coffee, served in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabic_coffee"] Arabic style, is the traditional
beverage but tea and various fruit juices are popular as well.[158] Arabic coffee is a
traditional beverage in Arabian cuisine. The earliest substantiated evidence of either
 coffee drinking or knowledge of the coffee tree is from the 15th century, in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sufi"] Sufi
monasteries of Arabia.
Sport 
 Arabic coffee is a
traditional beverage in
Arabian cuisine
 Football is the national sport in Saudi Arabia. The Saudi Arabia national
football team is considered one of Asia's most successful national teams,
having reached a joint record 6 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AFC_Asian_Cup"] AFC Asian Cup finals, winning three of those
finals (1984, 1988, and 1996) and having qualified for the World Cup four
 consecutive times ever since debuting at the 1994 tournament.In the 1994
FIFA World Cup under the leadership of Jorge Solari, Saudi Arabia beat both
Belgium and Morocco in the group stage before falling to defeat Sweden in
the round of 16. During the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1992_King_Fahd_Cup"] 1992 FIFA Confederations Cup, which was
played in Saudi Arabia, the country reached the final, losing 1–3 to 
Uruguay – Saudi Arabia match at the
 2018 FIFA World Cup in Russia
Argentina.Scuba diving, windsurfing, sailing and basketball (which is played
by both men and women) are also popular with the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi_Arabia_national_basketball_team"] Saudi Arabian national basketball team winning bronze at the
 1999 Asian Championship.[652][653][654] More traditional sports such as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Horse_racing"] horse racing and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Camel_racing"] camel racing are also
popular. A stadium in Riyadh holds races in the winter. The annual King's Camel Race, begun in 1974, is one of the
sport's most important contests and attracts animals and riders from throughout the region. Falconry, another
traditional pursuit, is still practised.[158]
Women's sport is controversial due to the suppression of female participation in sport by conservative Islamic
religious authorities,[655] however this restriction has eased slightly in recent years.[656][657][658] Until 2018 women
were not permitted in sport stadiums. Segregated seating, allowing women to enter, has been developed in three
stadiums across major cities.[659]
Saudi Arabia, in its vision for modernization, introduced the nation to a number of international sporting events,
bringing sports stars to the Kingdom. However, in August 2019, the kingdom's strategy received criticism for
appearing as a method of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sportswashing"] sportswashing soon after Saudi's US-based 2018 lobbying campaign foreign registration
documentations got published online. The documents showed Saudi Arabia as allegedly implementing a
'sportswashing' strategy, inclusive of meetings and official calls with supreme authorities of associations like the
Major League Soccer (MLS), World Wrestling Entertainment (WWE), National Basketball Association (NBA). The
strategy is being viewed as a method of sportswashing following the chaos spread across Yemen for 6 years.[660]
TV and Media
Television was introduced in Saudi Arabia in 1954. Saudi Arabia is a major market for pan-Arab satellite and pay-
TV. Among the major Saudi-owned broadcasting companies are the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MBC_Group"] Middle East Broadcasting Center, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rotana_Group"] Rotana and
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi_Broadcasting_Authority"] Saudi Broadcasting Authority which control a large share of the pan-Arab broadcasting market.[661] The Saudi
government closely monitors media and restricts it under official state law. Changes have been made to lessen theserestrictions; however, some government-led efforts to control information have also drawn international attention. As
of 2022, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reporters_Without_Borders"] Reporters Without Borders rates the Kingdom's press "Very Serious" situation.[662]
Page 34
Most of the early [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Newspapers"] newspapers in the Persian Gulf region were established in
Saudi Arabia.[663] The first newspaper founded in the country and in the Persian
Gulf area is [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Fallah"] Al Fallah, which was launched in 1920,[663] and the first English-
language newspaper is [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_News"] Arab News, which was launched in 1975.[664] All of the
newspapers published in Saudi Arabia are privately owned.[665]
 Saudi Arabia received access to the Internet in 1994.[666] According to World
Bank, as of 2020, 98% of the population of Saudi Arabia are Internet users
which puts it in the 8th rank among countries with the highest percentage of
internet users.[667] Saudi Arabia has one of the fastest [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/5G"] 5G internet speeds in the
world.[668][669] Saudi Arabia is the 27th largest market for [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/E-commerce"] e-commerce with a
revenue of US$8 billion in 2021, placing it ahead of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Belgium"] Belgium and behind
Norway.[670]

Notes
a. The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shahada"] Shahādah (Statement of faith) is sometimes translated into English as 'There is no god but Allah',
using the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romanization"] romanization of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabic_language"] Arabic word [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allah"] Allāh instead of its translation. The word Allāh (Arabic: ‎ٱلله)
literally translates as the God, as the prefix 'Al-' is the definite article.[2][3][4]
b. There is a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Consultative_Assembly_of_Saudi_Arabia"] Consultative Assembly, or Shura Council, which has no legislative power.[10] As its role is
only consultative it is not considered to be a legislature.[11]
c. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA/English"] /ˌsɔːdi əˈreɪbiə/ (  listen), [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA/English"] /ˌsaʊ-/ (  listen); Arabic: ‎ة ‎َّي ‎ِد ‎ْو ‎ُع ‎ٱلُّس As-Suʿūdīyah
d. Arabic: ‎ة ‎َّي ‎ِد ‎ْو ‎ُع ‎ٱلُّس ‎ة ‎َّي ‎ِب ‎َر ‎َع ‎ٱْل ‎ة ‎َك ‎َل ‎ْم ‎َم ‎ٱْل al-Mamlakah al-ʿArabīyah as-Suʿūdīyah,  pronunciation 
e. A number of Muslims, using justifications from the Quran,[565][566][567] insist that Islam did not begin
with Muhammad, but that it represents even previous [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prophet"] Prophets such as Abraham,[568][569][570][571]
who is credited with having established the sanctuary of Mecca.[572][573][574]
